<Author>canadianeh2007
<Content>It wasn't so bad I went to LTI for one week in mid-June with my wife and 15-year old daughter. We had gone to many 4-star hotels in the past, and this was our fourth time in Punta Cana. I have used reviews from this website to do research in the past, so I want to offer some information to prospective hotel guests. My family and I were very open-minded and tried to stay positive and ignore the small details that we did not find to our liking. Room: we stayed in building 5 with poolview. When we arrived, the air conditioning was not working and the balcony door was broken, so we went back to the reception and asked for a new room. We were promptly given the room next door, which was much better. We had been thinking of getting an oceanview room, but we didn't think it was worth it because we already spent so much time on the beach and the view of the pool and garden was very nice. The bathroom is small, making you feel claustrophobic when sitting on the toilet because the wall is inches from your face. The door to the bathroom, oddly enough, has a window, making it feel somewhat awkward even if you are sharing the hotel room with family. The air conditioning, though functioning in this room, leaked a bit in the bathroom. The room itself is livable, but the pillows are so lumpy, like a heap of socks rolled in a case, so bring your own. Beach: we have absolutely no complaints about the beach. It was spectacular! There was a bar nearby to hydrate you and plentiful palapas that offered a good amount of shade. The water was nice and warm, mostly clear, and the sand was fine and white. The weather was beautiful, so we spent most of the day on the beach. There is a small shopping area nearby where you can buy souvenirs. The beach is long enough to walk to your heart's content, but watch out for the annoying people selling time-shares. Pool: we didn't spend any time at the pool, but it was relatively big and had many chairs by it.  Food: we didn't go to any 脿 la carte restaurants and chose instead to go to the buffet restaurant. While the food got a bit same-ish after a few days, it was pretty good with something for everyone. Sometimes it was over or undercooked, and not all dishes looked appealing. We were lucky to not get sick, maybe because we avoided the salad bar. On out last night there was a Dominican holiday, and a big gala dinner was held outdoors by the pool area. It was very decorative and exciting, with a big cauldron-like pot bubbling over a fire to a roasted pig! There was some music accompanying, and the whole evening was full of entertainment. The food selection was excellent this time. Service: tipping is a tricky practice in hotels, and this was no exception. We left a dollar for the maid every day so that she would make our rooms nicely and we still had to remind the reception that we need 3 towels to be sent to the room and not 2. We occasionally tipped the waiters, but not many of them deserved it. We were treated reasonably well in the restaurants, but the lobby bar was a whole different story. There was only one bartender who would ignore you. Sometimes, though, you would just have to endure a line for drinks. Overall, most of the staff and fellow guests were friendly enough  *** Up until the end of our stay, we would have given the hotel 4 stars because it was a good value and had lovely beach. However, on Friday, large groups of Dominican families came to the resort. This influx of locals, we were told, was because of a Dominican holiday and they were given much cheaper rates than regular guests. Somewhere around 50-80 people came, and the resort turned into a madhouse. You couldn't get any peace and quiet. They choked off the service at bars and restaurants by overpowering other guests. They were unhygienic, with women and children ignoring the tongs at the buffet and taking food with their hands, licking their fingers blatantly. The children were throwing up, screaming, and running around unsupervised. We do take into consideration cultural differences, but this was something else! Luckily, we left soon after they came. Overall, we give the resort 3.5 stars, though it does have good potential to be 4.

<Author>TNTfab40
<Content>You get what you pay for... I too read all the mixed reviews and went on this trip with an open mind and positive attitude. This was an annual girls trip, we have both been to AI's in Mexico, first time to PC. This is rather long, but I researched extensively using this site and like to share info b/c of the help it was to me before I left.Since there is always something positive to find, especially on a long anticipated vacation, I will say that the resort is very clean, the grounds are pretty, the beach is beautiful, and the pina colodas are delicious. The rooms are like everyone has said, basic but fine for the few hours you sleep in them. We never had a problem w/ the room being cleaned, fresh towels, nice little touches like flowers left on the table (yes we tipped and left little gifts for the maid). The half hour catamarn ride is really nice. We also took the kayaks out and had fun with those.Unfortunately for us several negatives outweighed the positives. We REALLY tried to like the food. It became a running joke, TODAY we'll find something awesome to eat!! Trust me we tried everything. It may be a western palate thing, b/c the German tourists seemed to love the food. Things were over/under cooked, dry, watery, and just plain bland. I am perfectly happy seasoning my own food but there was just salt, pepper, and hotsauce. Some ketchup/mustard at the grill. Not a drop of BBQ, salsa, sour cream, something....please. And I can see how this could be the thing to do in order to not waste food, but the meats were not dressed like we're used too. Pork w/ pig skin still stuck to it, beef w/ bones/marrow/tendons the whole shebang. Anatomy lessons while you eat! We would laugh and name the dishes...deep fried cream filled mystery ball, beaks and tallons stew, marrow mush. I read about the lack of cream for coffee and we quickly learned to ask for leche, lots of leche. The coffee is STRONG and bitter. Probably fine if you like espresso. The bread, pasta bar, and stirfry were the most edible. And the fresh fruits and juices were great, but you can only eat so much fruit and bread. The ala cartes were better, pizza and salad in the Italian place was ok. I paid for a shrimp dinner the last night just to have some protein and that was pretty good. Soup, salad, 12 shrimp, veggies, and dessert for about $10.Apparently it was a Dominican holiday while we were there. The second day 5 busloads of Dominican families arrived. In itself that would be fine, the more the merrier, meet new people, experience new cultures, but read on for more about that. Since this is a small resort there was NO WHERE to go for quiet adult time. It looked like Disneyland, strollers everywhere, pool filled with blow up toys, kids running, screaming, throwing sand, falling asleep on the lobby couch and having an accident (I witnessed this). I have kids, I work with kids, I take a vacation with my kids, I don't let them throw sand and put them in a position where they could have an accident on a public couch. And b/c of the volume of people quality of service just plummeted. No silverware, cups, towels, crowds at the bar where it felt like the stock trading pit trying to get the bartenders attention b/c no one knew how to line up. If you could yell your order in Spanish and push your way to the front you got your drink.Which leads me to the last and most upsetting (for us) negative that pretty much sealed our feelings/rating about the LTI. We tip. Well. We started right out of the box tipping the bartender for our first round of drinks. At this point it was still quiet, so not a lot of tourists to remember. The very next round we were ignored, then rushed thru (pointing at you and snapping). This progressed over the days to pointing at us and saying hurry up lady. Despite tipping before and after service. So after 3 days we just stopped tipping. Of course on the last day, as we're wheeling our luggage thru the lobby, everyone wants to know why we're leaving, when we're coming back, that now we're Dominican family, yeah, right. Thru out we thought there was some kind of negative vibe from the staff and other guests. At first we chalked it up to language barriers/culture. We were smiling, saying hello in Spanish/German, making eye contact, tyring to be nice and generally got a blank stare in return. Occasional hola from some staff. (except for Theresa at the horseback riding hut, she was very nice) One night we sat in the lobby bar just talking and laughing and when we got up to leave the table next to us basically made fun of us like a bunch of middle school kids (imitated us laughing and talking). We had a couple drinks, not loud and drunk by any means. At least three times we heard Americano with some snide eye roll, comment after we walked by with our attempt at saying hi (this from German tourists). Half way thru a woman approached me at the disco and said she just wanted to say hi b/c she could tell I was another American and that no one else would talk to her. The last day we watched a group of 5 girls have a tiff w/ some staff by the pool. They were told they had to move so the pool could be cleaned. There were acres of empty chairs to the right and left, but these 5 chairs had to be moved. You could tell these girls had had it and refused to move. We went up to them and sure enough, American women on a girls trip. They said there were treated rudely thruout. Coin purse stolen w/ room key, charged $10 for new key, told they couldn't get towels until 2pm when they were available at 8:30am, staff actually mocking them behind their backs. (one spoke Spanish and knew what they were doing). And an hour after being told to move, nobody even attempting to clean the pool. The last day I was so ready to leave. Checked out and was told the charge was $32 for 5 days safe rental, one local phone call, and the shrimp dinner. I paid in US, went to breakfast, then really looked at the bill. Computer print out on the bottom had all the conversions. The bill was $21.49 US. That did it for me. I went back and pitched a fit, the guy at the checkout first said that he said $22, denied I paid him $32, said there were only 2 10's in the drawer, then magically just threw me a $10 when I started asking for a manager. When I spoke with the manager at the desk, he suddenly had very limited English. And couldn't get a hold of the English speaking German manager. Since we were leaving in 15 mins I just let it go. At that point I couldn't wait to leave. We ran into a handful of American couples that did not have as much hassle. Leads me to wonder that women traveling alone are targeted or something. Obviously this is not a place we would return to. I would give PC/Dominican another chance b/c it is so pretty, the tour we went on was wonderful (Mt. View safari), and other American tourists at the airport had glowing reports about different resorts.We booked this vacation with a budget in mind and it was very cheap. As in you get what you pay for cheap. Next time I'll spend the extra buck and go somewhere where I can eat and at least feel welcomed. In closing our mottos for the LTI.LTI, where the food Lacks Taste Incredibly and where we Like To Intimidate Americans.

<Author>mondaysme
<Content>Beautiful Grounds - Rooms OK - Food Average With this resort, you get what you pay for. We got a great deal out of Atlanta. If you get a good deal, by all means - go and enjoy yourself! The resort grounds are beautiful and very tropical! Some of the best we saw. We walked around and looked at neighboring resorts and found our resort's grounds to be nicer even though some resorts were much more expensive. The rooms are not nearly as nice as you would expect based on the grounds, but they are OK. We had 2 double beds and could not upgrade to a king. When we first arrived the deadbolt wouldn't work and the sliding glass door wouldn't lock or slide. We reported it to the bellboy - don't waste your breath! He'll take your tip and say I'll send someone up and you'll never see him again. So then we called the front desk. Said that they would send someone right up. We waited and hour and then went down to the front desk. Finally, they sent someone up and both were fixed within 2 hours of arriving but obviously you have to stay after them. Then they came back in the morning to fix the locks - I guess they don't communicate with each other very well since they didn't know it was fixed the day before. So if something is broken, don't give up, just keep bothering them until they fix it. These were the only major issues with our stay. As for Punta Cana, the beaches are fantastic! But there isn't really a town nearby so most people never leave the resorts. If you do go into town, hire a guide. There are no street signs, you will be very obvious as a tourist, and they drive like the drivers in Rio or some other big city with very limited trafic control . This is a developing nation. Therefore, it is very, very poor. If you're there on vacation - then you have far more money than most of these people will ever have - so be generous - tip them! Yes, it's an all inclusive resort but a couple of dollars will go very far with them. We tip the bartender a total of about $12 over 5 days and he got my husband a 6 pack Brahama Beer in bottles! I travel for a living and had tons of hotel shampoos, lotions, and soaps. I left some each day for the maid along with a dollar or two and we always had Cokes and water in the mini fridge. When we went into town, I took a bag of these items and gave them to the shoe shine boys for their families. Everyone was very pleased and this cost me nothing but made them happy. These items are expensive and lotion is a considered luxury - so most families can't afford it. The food is fine..not great.. not bad. The seafood restaurant is good but only the pay entrees like lobster (reasonable in price and very good). The buffets are fine and offer a good variety. The egg guy was very nice. The pizza was not very good. Breakfast was excellent. Lunch and dinner OK. Everyone should be able to find something to eat.I enjoyed the trip, but I prefer to visit places where I can experience the culture and not feel isolated and removed from the people. I consider Punta Cana to be like Cancun - too designed and created only for tourism. It is nicer and much prettier than Cancun but still designed mostly for Europeans and Americans. Go enjoy your vacation but don't expect first class while paying for coach!

<Author>Dartmouth7
<Content>Great Vacation My husband and I spent last week at the LTI, and can't say enough good about it. The resort was beautiful - the vegetation very mature and exceptionally maintained.The beach is second to none, and this resort is located on a very good section of the beach. They certainly add to the enjoyment of your vacation. I had heard mixed reviews about the Dominicans, but if this resort is any indication, they are wonderful people and made you feel welcome.The food was quite good- yes it's different than America, but isn't that why you travel? To encounter other cultures? If you want fast food for supper, stay in the US. One thing we really enjoyed was lots of fresh and very tasty lettuce and tomatoes- something we have yet to encounter in Cuba. I have to say I was a little disappointed in the a la cartes. There really is only one, where you sit at a table and are waited on. The Italian restaurant, while very good, was mostly a buffet at supper time too. My only complaint was that the wine was watered down. Sometimes it was better than others.One thing we really liked was that you could book your a la cartes in the morning each day, so if there was room , you could eat at one every night if you wanted to.Having said this, the buffet was probably one of the best we've had- lots of choice, and many dishes unique to the Dominican, if you wanted to try something different. The strengths are in the chicken and pork- any beef I sampled was quite tough and chewy.There were plenty of loungers at the beach and the pool- it was never a problem getting one regardless of the time you got there.It was very hot the week we were there, and there are always lots of tiki huts to provide shade.The rooms were quite adequate,basic but clean.All in all, we had a very enjoyable vacation, great value for the money and would return in a heartbeat.

<Author>Sundra
<Content>Amazing Just got back from an amazing week at LTI. We've never been to Dominican so didn't know what to expect and after reading some reviews we were a bit worried. The flight with Skyservice was tight but uneventful. We quickly got through customs at the Punta Cana airport and the shuttle to LTI was waiting. Everone on the bus was going to LTI so is was a straight run - seems like a 20 minute ride. Got to the resort and entered the beautiful foyer, checked in, were greeted with a drink by a waitress and headed off to our room. The room was very clean and nice. We changed and headed to the pool and were pleased with the lush green gardens. Two pools, lots of lawn chairs and tiki huts to sit under. Shade was needed by late morning/noon and we managed to find it everyday. We headed to the beach which is only a stones throw from the pool and found paradise. Beautiful white flour soft sand and tall green palm trees swaying in the warm tropical breeze. Very clean shoreline and water that was beautiful and tourquoise.. Again lots of lawn chairs. Tiki huts everywhere and we always seemed to find one. The restaurants were awesome. Excellent food and variety. It seemed the food and drinks never stopped. The main buffet always had fresh omelets for breakfast and everything else imaginable. Lunch may as well have been dinner there was so much food and dinner was wonderful. If by chance you get bored of the buffet, there is a wonderful smaller buffet right by the beach that serves breakfast lunch and dinner. They always seem to have the grill going barbequing burgers/dogs/sausages/chicken and for dinner they add roast beef, steak, pork, fish and have pasta and salads at the buffet. The Italian restaurant was very nice and had awesome lasagna and good pizza and wonderful lemon lime icecream that puts a refreshing end to your meal. There is a seafood restaurant we didn't get to. We were allowed to go to the alacarte restaurants everynight if we wanted - you just reserve in the morning.There was lots of fun to be had with the fun games that the staff put on and we enjoyed the banana boat, catarmaran and kayaks. Excursions were offered however our Sunquest Rep was never around so we couldn't book with him, however, the resort offers the same excursions.The weather was great, nice and warm and a beautiful breeze. It did rain most days in the afternoon but this was a nice relief from the blazing sun.Finally the wonderful Dominican people who work at the resort. They couldn't have been more friendly, happy and energetic. They are there to please you and are very pleasant and kind. Service was excellent! My husband and I took our two teens and none of us wanted to come home. We'd go back to LTI and Punta Cana tomorrow if we could. We highly recommend LTI.

<Author>sferge
<Content>Awesome Place My best friend and I just got back to Chicago, IL last night from a 6 day stay in Punta Cana at the LTI. We booked through cheap caribbean.com (great place to book travel and excellent prices). I have traveled many places outside the US and after we booked our trip my g-friend starting reading horrible things about the hotel; none of which are true. The staff was very friendly (a please and a thank you go along way), the rooms are very clean never had a problem with the towels or the pillows probably due to the fact that we tipped the maid everyday - well worth the money each day.(that is if you tip your maid $4.00 (US) a day). Be sure to bring your own travel mug as the glasses are very small and dont keep your drinks cold. The grounds were nicely kept (some spots could of used a coat of paint such as the patio railing, however keep in mind that Punta Cana is in the hurricane zone - and many other resorts look the same) the pool was very clean. The food was good (the italian and the poolside grill were the best). International was okay, its a buffet people it is what it is. Bring bug spray, sunscreen, travel mugs, a travel iron as they do not provide them. Have fun and enjoy LTI as I would return to this resort.

<Author>Sol_survivor
<Content>LTI - Great value for the right price Just returned from a week at LTI 鈥?Punta Cana, March 11 鈥?18, 2007 and had a very enjoyable time. As most of the postings are correct, we will add or confirm a few of our own experiences: Arrival: Getting through the airport on arrival was fairly simple and quick. The resort is about 30 minutes from the airport, but with all of the stops to drop off guests at other resorts, the trip is well over an hour. Resort: A bit 鈥渢ired鈥?looking but clean. The grounds were nice with lots of flowering bushes and palm trees. Expect about 70% or more of the guest to be German. Mainly adults, few kids, mainly around the pool during the day.Tennis courts: If you are looking to play lots of tennis on your vacation, you鈥檒l be disappointed. There are just 2 concrete courts covered with course sand. Guess it is a Caribbean version of 鈥渃lay courts鈥? There are 2 resort organized tournaments, a singles tournament on Thursday and a doubles on Saturday. Four people turned up for the singles鈥?tournament. We passed on the doubles. Racquets and balls are available, free of charge. Room: We arrived at the resort at approximately 11:30 AM and our room was not available until about 1:00 PM. We had lunch and returned to the check-in counter and were advised that the room was still not available but would be by 7:30 PM. However; because of the inconvenience, we were upgraded from a garden view room to an ocean view room and the charge for the room safe (US$2 per day/US$14 per week) was being waived. This was offered without us asking and we were provided a courtesy suit to use to shower and change until the room was available at 7:30 PM.There is no iron in the room so walk with your own travel iron. There are 2 closets to hang your clothes.Bathroom: Hand wash gel was provided at the sink with body-wash/shampoo gel in the bath via dispensers. Bathroom supplies commonly provided such as wash cloths, Q-tips, sewing kits, combs, etc were not provided. Towels, although changed everyday, were grey and dingy. Security: We did not experience anything missing from our room.Beach: Great beach with lots of European sunbathing practiced. Resort was not at 100% capacity so there were no problems getting lounges regardless of when you hit the beach. Sea weed is raked up early every morning. The only problem we encountered was that it was very windy which blew sand into our eyes. Ocean was a bit choppy but was not a deterrent for swimmers. Lots of banana boat ($)  parasailing available ($).Restaurants: There are 4 restaurants in the resort. The main buffet, Italian, Seafood and Grill. Dinner reservations are required for the Seafood and Italian restaurants with 1 dinner reservation per restaurant per week allowed. The main buffet restaurant offered the 4 basics every night, i.e. pork, fish, beef  chicken. Generally, the meals were good but not great. We are picky eaters so you be the judge. There are 2 鈥渓obster nights鈥?at the grill, Monday and Friday nights. The price is US$17 per lb for the lobster which you pick after which it is weighed and grilled.The Grill uses real charcoal to cook burgers  hotdogs during the day and steaks, lobster, fish  chicken at night. I think it makes a big difference as the burgers  steaks were very good.Bars: There are bars in each restaurant plus one between the poll and the beach and one in the lobby. Had to leave the resort to get a cold beer as they were cool at best. No premium drinks, not even Brugal rum available. Just your basic 鈥渞ot-gut鈥?available. Smoking: Expect lots of cigar  cigarette smokers at the beach, pool, restaurants, theatre, etc. Expect a haze of smoke in the lobby on evenings. There was one buffet dining room that was smoke-free. Shopping: There is a free shuttle every 2 hours between 10:00 AM to 6:00 PM from the resort to the Real Palm shopping plaza. Forget about it! The shuttle takes close to an hour to get to the plaza which is only half occupied. The prices are ridiculous and there are only about 6 鈥?8 shops open, including a Tony Roma鈥檚 Restaurant. There are 2 flea markets within walking distance along the beach. As you step off the resort onto the beach, turn left and within 10 minutes there are a bunch of stalls right on the beach. Or you can turn right and walk for about 20 minutes until you reach the Captain Cook鈥檚 Seafood Restaurant. About 50 meters off the beach there is a strip on the road with various stores and a fair size supermarket. There are also flea market type shops around. You have to (and they expect you to) haggle with them. Go late in the afternoon at about 4:00 for the best prices. A 750ml Bermudez 12 year old rum went from US$45 to US$22 or US$40 for 2 bottles. Picked up 2 鈥?750ml bottles, Bacardi 151 and Brugal Anejo, for US$20. Also, a box of 25 Cohiba cigars (Cuban made) for US$35. For example, they wanted US$35 for the Bacardi 151 rum and we offered US$15. We agreed on US$20 for the Bacardi  Brugal. Activities: We did the ATV and horse-back riding tours. Reasonable priced but a very long ride to get to the ATVs or horse stable. An hour and a half trip each way is such a waste of time. Pool: There was a very large pool with lots of lounges usually available. We are not 鈥減ool people鈥?so we did not hang out around there.Gym: There is a well equipped gym next to the 鈥楳etamorphosis Spa鈥? Usually not busy on evenings. Should be a/conditioned as it is hot even when the windows are open. Spa: Great spa services available. Prices are equivalent to North American but the services are top-notch.Bugs: No mosquitoes when we were there. Did not hear anyone complain about bugs or mosquitoes, however, we don鈥檛 speak German so they could very well have been. Duty-free: There are only 2 good duty-free shops at the airport. Brugal Anejo rum at the airport ($20) is more expensive than at the resort! But the best place to shop is at the flee market on the beach.

<Content>Great relaxing clean resort My sister in law and I just returned from a week at the LTI, march 29 to april 5, 2007.We flew Air Transit direct from St. John's, NF to Punta Cana. Not much leg room on these flights but you make do. Dinner consisted of a turkey sandwich which was a little dry and they charge for snacks. I suggest you bring along a few snacks in your carry on. Same for the return trip.We arrived late evening with no delays at the airport. Luggage arrived quickly, no major line ups and smooth directions to your bus. There are people who will take your luggage if you wish, if not a polite no thank you worked. The bus is air conditioned and quite comfey and the drive is under 1 hour as we had two other hotels to stop at first.There was no waiting at the hotel for check in as there were only a few of us and the luggage was delivered to our room within 20 minutes. We were on the 2nd floor, building 5, which is the one next to the beach and close to the pool and bar/grill.the rooms safe is $2 us per day and you pick this up at the front desk along with the TV remote if you want one. You pick up your beach towels by the pool and you can exchange them every day.No complaints with the food as we always found something good to eat. There are 3 buffet resturants you can choose from and 1 ala carte. We did not try the ala carte as we did not want any fixed time for meals. The Grill is great both for lunch and dinner. Lunch time the food is cooked and you ask for want you want and in the evening you order and its cooked for you then. Always lots of veggies, fruits, breads and cheese. The BBQ chicken is excellent and the fries are great.Drinks were great and the beer was always cold. Each bar makes the drinks a little different. the lobby bar makes the best Miami Vice ( little rum). We used our thermal mugs for the beach and pool, this kept the drinks cold and sand free. We are tea drinkers and they only have the very small cups, so we used the thermal mugs for our tea in the am. Lots of different tea blends, but it won't hurt to bring your favorite.Beach was awesome, fine white sand as far as the eye could see and into the ocean so no shells to walk on, it eas great. they have a section roped off and is not too deep. Some waves and some seaweed however the seaweed was cleaned up every morning and if it washed ashore during the day, they came back and raked it up. You can walk for quite a distance both directions and no problems. You can view lots of the other resorts as you stroll along.Vendors were no problem and for the few we seen again a polite no thank was fine. There is a market to the left of the hotel ( facing the ocean) we you can barter and there are a few shops at the hotel, no bartering. One nite a few vendors set up by the show stage and they were not aggressive.There are time share people on the beach in front of the Club section and out side the main buffett. We only seen them during the week.Did not spend much time at the shows as we have been to Cuba and the DR before and they much the same. However we heard good review from some who attended.Staff were friendly and polite. This resort is small which makes it easy to get around and a chance to see the full resort. There was always lots to see at the beach as it is quite busy with water sports and people. From the looks of the kids at the resort they really enjoyed it also.The pool has two sections, shallow and deep divided by a bridge. there is a life guard on the shallow end were most of the kids hang out.Our room was clean on arrival and kept that way and we had no major problem with bugs. There are tiny flies in the evening and they do bite, so bring the bug spray and use it. Few bees and wasps around the pool area but not bothersome. Lots of plants and flowers on this resort so the land scape is beautiful.Lots of loungers and shady huts both at the pool and the beach but you have to be up early to snag a good spot with some shade.There is a disco but we did not go, our plan was to flake and bake so were we up early and turned in early. There are shops at the Punta Cana airport, but they are pricey and they do have duty free and a Wendys and a Baskin Robbins.Of note, Air Transit also offered duty free both ways, but selction is limited.WE both enjoyed this resort and would stay here again.

<Author>LYM19
<Content>Fantastic!!!!!! Just got back from a week's vacation from the DR. We stayed at the LTI and it was fabulous. The LTI is a smaller resort which to us was a plus. Most resorts are sooooooo large that you have to take a shuttle to the beach! The food was fine. The buffet is good and the Pizzaria is great. You don't always need a reservation. We even got a pizza to go and took it back to our room one night. I don't recommend the other a la carte restaurant. It was the fanciest but the worst. I got an upset stomach pretty bad one day but nothing that a little medicine didn't take care of. It was a fabulous afternoon.One thing we did when we went to the pool or beach was taking our ice bucket from our room. We got the bars to fill it up with ice and kept our drinks cool for longer and had extra ice when we needed it. A great little trick has been mentioned before but worth repeating. Your room card key goes into a slot in your room to turn on the power and air conditioner. When you leave the room you have to take your key so the air turns off. Take a rewards type card (not a credit card) and use it in the key slot to your room to keep the air conditioner on. I know some people that even used cardboard. Housekeeping does not remove them.Anyway, if your thinking about the LTI I would say you made a very good choice indeed!

<Author>TravelExpert-TA
<Content>LTI - Not that Great! We stayed at the LTI Beach Resort from Feb. 4-11, 2007 and after reading all of the reviews I was expecting something really good. However, this was not the case.The Positives:The resort size is great if you are someone like myself who is not crazy about the really massive resorts that take forever to get around. The LTI is a comfortable size and is easy to get around and definitely not too huge; it has a more intimate feel.The grounds have beautiful palm trees everywhere but do not have any flowers. The beach is great but then the beach is good pretty much in all of Punta Cana so it doesn't really matter too much which resort you stay at, although we found the beach to be really nice in front of the Paradisus and/or the Iberostar.Now for the negatives:The hotel is definitely more of a 3 star. The lobby is not all that impressive and this is your first impression of the the LTI so it really sets the tone. If you go there expecting a 3 star you will not be disappointed, however if you were told it is a 4 star (like myself) you will wonder why. The staff are not that friendly and except for the front desk most staff did not speak English which can be frustrating when trying to ask a question. Also, the service was very mediocre, they are definitely not willing to go that extra mile. I realize we have been spoiled with North American service being the best in the world but the service at LTI was the minimum you would expect.The worst thing really was the food!!! I have been to Cuba where the food is known not to be good but I was expecting more from Dominican however I would say the food was on par with Cuba if not worse. The good thing is that you probably won't gain any weight! I really can't understand how anyone can recommend the food. The only thing they can get right is chicken, that's about it.I know it's already been mentioned but this resort caters mostly to Germans and other Europeans and while I did not think this would matter before I went I now realize that this is definitely a negative. The Germans think they own the place and reserve every beach chair with their towels and think they can dissappear for the whole day and no one is allowed to move their things.The nightly entertainment was a joke. It was sometimes really embarrassing to watch as it was so bad but hey, at least you can leave if you don't like it. During the day however, the only time you can enjoy any peace and quiet while at the pool is between 12-3pm otherwise you will be bombarded with noise and music from the entertainment staff that can get incredibly annoying if all you want to do is relax and read your book. We had an oceanview room which was great and I would definitely recommend gettting one as this is a beautiful view. I did not find the pillows to be a problem as I was expecting after reading some of the reviews and the rooms were kept clean but are very basic. There is no coffeemaker in the room and the lighting is not good for reading or doing ones makeup. Bring your own facecloth if you use this to shower as they do not provide any. They do have hairdryers though, so don't bother packing one but they do not have an iron or ironing board in the room.Overall, we enjoyed Punta Cana but would not go back to the LTI Beach resort as I am sure you could stay at a nicer resort for only minimally more.

<Author>Nems
<Content>October 2006 - Disappointing My husband and I did not actually pay for our one-night stay at this LTI resort, as we were on a cancelled flight and Delta put all of us up at this place. I would not, however, pay to stay here, as I thought it sub-par, in comparison to my other all-inclusive experiences. I have stayed at Paradisus and Secrets resorts and had only positive experiences. LTI is a few steps below those places, and I did not find much that I found positive. The room was small, and not entirely clean. There was trash on the counters. We could not find a remote for the TV, although we later heard we could have picked one up at the front desk, which seems odd. Our room was beside a small road, which alternated between ATVs loudly whizzing by (even in the middle of the night), or pesticide trucks spraying disgusting clouds of insecticide. The pillows seemed to consist of small and large lumps of foam, smashed together into a pillowcase, which was the equivalent of sleeping on soft potatoes. Besides those issues, I have a problem with the resort labeling itself as all inclusive, since many things were not, in fact, included. The safe in the room, for example, can be used for an extra fee, although ours didn't even have a door on it. Out of the four restaraunts on the property, only one is actually included, and it is a terrible buffet. Service at the buffet is iffy at best, and once we went the entire meal without even being served water. I believe that some beer, wine, and liquor is included, although those were never offered to me by the waiters in the buffet (they never even spoke to us, just plopped a water glass down). However, most decent alcoholic drinks are not included. Perhaps if someone who has not been to other all-inclusive resorts were to stay here, it would not seem as bad as it did to me (although in discussing the resort with others on our cancelled flight, they all shared the same sentiments). Maybe it is a decent resort for families with children. But I would not not recommend it for couples wanting a romantic getaway. Look at Paradisus (children allowed) or Secrets (couples only) instead.

<Author>Glamor1014
<Content>July 9-16, 2006 My boyfriend and I stayed at the LTI from July 9-16th. We are both 30 years old.I had visited Punta Cana in 2004 and stayed at the Paradisus Punta Cana (amazing resort) so this was my second time visiting. I love Punta Cana because of the warm weather, the cool breeze and the warm ocean water!I read all the reviews for LTI (daily) and was somewhat nervous to stay, but I found that it was an average hotel with no major problems. The airport is small but not scary at all. You get off the plane and are hit with hot humid weather! Wear shorts on the flight! You will have to walk from the plane to immigration outside in the heat! Be aware that the second you get through baggage you are going to be pulled in many different directions by taxi drivers that want your money. Do not let anyone take your bag unless you plan on tipping them. When we arrived at the hotel we found that they were really busy and didn鈥檛 really go out of their way to make us feel welcome. No one came over to us to help us with our bags until after we checked in and we never got our welcome drink that was promised. We asked for a king size bed and they told us that a room with one bed was an upgrade because they only had an ocean view left. They gave the room without an extra charge, but we had to wait 30 minutes get into it.Our bags were brought up about 10 minutes after got into our room and we tipped $2.The room was plain, nothing special, but clean and we had an ocean view. We used a grocery store card to keep the air conditioning on all day and the room stayed comfortable. There are also English speaking TV channels. We tipped the maid $2 every day and she kept the room clean and the refrigerator stocked.The food was somewhat of a problem for me, although my BF had no problems finding something he liked so I guess I am just a picky eater. The meat does not taste normal so I stayed away from the hamburgers and hotdogs. They had chicken everyday at the poolside grill and in the buffet and that was the best chicken! It almost tastes like Boston Market! We never made reservations at any of the restaurants because they were always booked by the time we arrived for breakfast.The pool was always very warm and we never had a problem getting a seat. We would just put our towels on chairs when we went to breakfast. We also left our beach bag at our seat while we were gone and there were no problems. The Beach is beautiful and again, we never had a problem finding a chair. We did get a hut two days, but only when we put our towels down before breakfast. Of you want a hut, get out there early! Getting towels was a little confusing the first day. You will get your towel next at the pool (up where the ping pong table is) and then you can replace the towels when you want. However, they are not always there so you should get one in the morning each day.The shows were just ok. The dance club doesn鈥檛 open until 11:00 PM so the shows are really the only thing to do at night. They do not speak in English but they try to do dance shows or shows that get the audience involved that don鈥檛 involve a lot of speaking. They let the kids go up on stage and perform from 8:00 PM 鈥?9:00 PM and that was really cute. It is all part of the Kids Club that the hotel offers. The kids had a BALL. The kids have a GREAT time at this resort so if you have younger children, this is a great place to stay.This is a family resort and had a lot of kids while we were there. We met another couple on an excursion that was on their honeymoon and they were booked at LTI but changed hotels as there were too many kids. If you are looking for a resort without kids, LTI is not the resort for you. We did only 1 excursion, but it was worth every penny! We did the Bavaro 4x4鈥檚. It was $55 a person to share an ATV. This excursion takes you on the beach where there are jumps set up. It was a lot of fun! We did an afternoon excursion which I suggest as I think they can be flexible about how long you are out. The only other thing that I can comment on is the alcoholic beverages. I have stayed at other all-inclusive resorts in the past and they usually have a drink list or special drinks that you can order. LTI only had beer, wine, Pina Colada and Strawberry Banana smoothies. I am not a big drinker, so I didn鈥檛 know what to order and what was an extra charge (some alcohol was additional) so I drank Pina Coladas all week. Also, when ordering these types of drinks, you must specify that you want alcohol in it, if not, they will just give you a regular drink. We actually felt that we weren鈥檛 served very quickly when we would go to a bar. Some other couples told us that you need to tip a certain bartender first, and then he will take care of you all vacation.

They are very family oriented and if you treat them well they will show you their kindness. But if your hateful you will get the service you deserve!!! Some of the reviews say there is no entertainment!!! Every night at 9:30 they had a great show. <Author>jjff
<Content>Enjoyed our stay Hello,I stayed at the LTI Beach Resort from April 15th to the 22nd and had a great time. I was actually quite scared to go after reading some of the reviews on this website so I thought I would add a positive one and let people know my honest opinion. I travelled with 8 other people and we all enjoyed ourselves. We are ranging in age from 26-29 and have all travelled down south in the past to all-inclusives in Cuba, Puerto Plata, Jamaica and Mexico and the LTI rated well among them. I feel it has earned its 4.5 star rating. Check in: Quick and easy, the front desk staff were friendly. Although we were a bit disappointed that they did not allow us to have a late check-out. We had to use their courtesy room the last day to shower. It was fine but we would have preferred to stay in our own roomsRooms: Spacious and clean. The bathroom is marble, very nice, good lighting. There is a window in the door but it is not a big deal as the toilet is tucked to one side. The showers are great with a removable shower head (it was attached to a hose so you could take it down) I found that great for removing sand at the end of the day. There was always lots of hot water. Each room has a balcony with chairs, a table and 2 lines for hangining clothes (very handy). Each room also has a fridge and it is stocked with water and pop dailyService: Excellent!! The maids were great, very sweet, keeping the rooms very clean, stocking with as many towels and bottles of water you requested. We never had to buy bottled water because if you saw a maid in the hall with her cart, she would give you as many bottles of water as you asked for. The service at the bars and restaurants were also great, very friendly, always prompt, very professional.Food: Great. I was never hungry and never afraid to eat. Breakfasts were excellent, delicious donuts, omlettes, pancakes, french toast, boiled eggs, breads, fruits, milkshakes, bacon, sausage, scrambled eggs - pretty much anything you could ask for. Lunch was also delicious; you could eat at the beach bar, where they served burgers, chicken, french fries, sandwichs and sweets. You could also eat at the italian restaurant where they served pizza, salad, pasta, sweets, fruits etc... Or you could eat at the main buffet. Dinner was also good. The main buffet has a pasta station, stir-fry station, fish station, meat station (they had lamb, roast beef, turkey, chicken; a different cut of meat each day). We ate at each of the a la cartes as well. The seafood restaurant gives you choice of fish, beef or chicken. You also get a choice of a crab or garden salad and they bring a dessert cart around. I had the crab salad, fish and tiramisu and it was delicious! They do have menu you can order from that you have to pay extra for but we all enjoyed the meals that were included. The Italian restaurant turns into a a la carte in the evening and offers pizza, pasta, and sweets. We found it pretty good. The pizza is better quality that the pizza you get at lunch (more toppings) and it was nice to not eat at the buffet every night.One complaint I did have about the food was the 24 hour snacks. They only had sandwiches and soup after 11pm. We were disappointed because in other resorts we could get french fries, burgers etc... They did have burgers and fries up until 11pm but after that only sandwiches and soup. A few times we came back from the disco a bit hungry but luckily brought our own snacks. Beach: Beautiful, I spoke with one of the staff at the watersport centre and he said the beach spans for 50+ km. All you can see is beach. There were plenty of chairs, though sometimes it was hard to find a chair in the shade. You had to get up early to put your towel on one. The signs say you are not allowed to do this but we figured that if you can't beat them you might as well join them. We played a lot of beach volleyball, went boogey boarding every day, brought frisbees etc... so we were very entertained; the days went by too quickly. They also had activities on the beach, sand castle competition, dance lessons, aerobics and every day they played a different crazy game. Entertainment: The anamacion staff were very friendly and sweet; you can see they work hard. We only saw 2 shows in the evening; karaoke and dancers from Santo Domingo. Both were good. The Disco is pretty small and was not busy while we were there. However, where we were a group of 9, we made our own fun and always had a good time there. As well, we met up with another group of Canadians there who came to the disco with us a few nights. Atmosphere: There were a lot of Europeans and Germans at this resort but it is German-owned. There were also quite a few Canadians. I thought it was neat to have people from different cultures because you get to see how similiar we all are. Even though we don't speak the same language, we all come down south for fun and relaxation in the sun and that was what we all recieved!Overall we enjoyed our stay. If you booked a trip to the LTI, don't worry; it has everything you need and if you have reasonable expectations you will not be disappointed.

<Author>vivacaciones
<Content>Very nice place, though more for families than couples My wife and I just returned from the DR, we were there from April 13 - April 21, though we only stayed at LTI for four days. The positives include:The stretch of beach the LTI is on is absolutely beautiful, white sands, clear blue water, wonderful weather. The facilities are very clean and modern, the reception hall is beautiful, the pool is segmented so there鈥檚 a kiddy pool, a Jacuzzi and an adult pool, lots of lounge chairs and shades on the beach front, and the grounds well kept with lots of tropical plants. A few different spots to relax with a drink or grab a meal. If you want to use their gym you must wear gym clothes and sneakers or they鈥檒l kick you out. That happened to us!In general, the staff were friendly and helpful. Most know enough to communicate in several languages - English, Spanish, French, and German being the most typical. We have never stayed at an all inclusive, so it was wonderful to eat all we wanted, get drinks whenever we wanted, try a few water activities and never pick up our wallet. There are some pay options for additional activities and meals, but we didn't bother.There were a variety of activities led by the animation team like beach aerobics, games, dancing. And nightly activities, like a live band one night, a dance performance on two different nights, and a karaoke show. There was also a night club - though it tended to be populated by teens and reggeaton music, so we didn't go back. We had gone to the DR planning to dance lots of merengue and salsa which didn鈥檛 happen with the type of music played at the disco. How ironic.The slightly less positives include:We prefer to experience as much of a culture as possible, so we were glad that we traveled around the DR before ending up at LTI, because LTI is fairly far removed from the rest of Dominican life (though I suppose most resorts at Punta Cana are). As many people have said, the largest population at the resort are couples and families from Germany. My wife and I both speak Spanish, but my high school German came in handy more than anything else.There are tons of kids. If you are a family looking for a relaxing experience, then this is the place - they seemed to have lots of activities to keep the kids interested. But if you're a couple looking for a romantic rendezvous, just know there will be little feet running everywhere. It wasn't bad, per se, but you definitely know it is a family resort.I don't know if I should call the food less positive or positive. I disagree with some of the other reviews saying it was terrible. It wasn't. We're from New York City, the restaurant capital of the world, we think we know great food, and yes, LTI's meals weren't five star, but for an all-inclusive/buffet-style atmosphere I think they did fairly well. Yes, it is true, most options repeat themselves each night, but the chefs do make an effort to change them up a bit. For example, fish was available every night, but sometimes it was breaded and fried or made with an almond cream sauce or grilled or poached. And there are many, many options. Plus there are four places to eat (two of which you do have to pay extra - we didn't eat at those, but I supposed that offers more options). Fresh fruit everyday and every meal was a huge plus and we felt we were able to have enough choice. When my wife asked what I thought of the food, I did often reply, yeah, it's okay. So no, I didn't feel like I was eating at the 21 Club, but I totally disagree that it was terrible. In fact, now that we are home and have to cook for ourselves and buy our own meals, we REALLY miss it!It is important to know that there is a timeshare building on the premises called the Cayena and yes, nice men in yellow shirts wait outside of the main food hall and walk the beach trying to interest people in a tour. So you know what we did, we just avoided them. Simple as that. We wish they weren't there, but they weren't pushy - in fact they never spoke to us.Needless to say Punta Cana and LTI in general are not easy to get to, we came from Santo Domingo and two buses and a cab ride later we arrived. I'm not sure what the experience would be like if you flew straight into the Punta Cana airport. If you're up for adventure, our bus rides were actually not so bad - we took a coach style bus from Santo Domingo to Higuey [RD$150 pp, about 2.5 hours] and then transferred to a guaga style bus to Bavaro Plaza [RD$60 pp, 45 min] and then cabbed it to LTI [the cab was aimed at tourists and so charged RD$150 to go 5 minutes]. There are NO buses to Punta Cana from Santo Domingo or Santiago, so it takes some work, but for us it was a good and safe experience, although it was somewhat tiring. We were also winging it; not knowing exactly how to get there, how much it would cost, nor the prices we would be charged.. My wife is Hispanic and took care of all the transactions and haggling, questions etc鈥?Thank goodness because no one spoke English outside of the resort and it may be a bit overwhelming for non-Spanish speakers to try. It would probably be better to fly straight into Punta Cana to avoid the hassle of getting there from Santiago or Santo Domingo. We do have a few complaints:It seems that the LTI contains NO non-smoking rooms, or so we were told. This was a big draw back for us. Though, on the brighter side, the housekeeping service did their best to change all of our bedding and even sprayed our room to try and get the smell out. It helped a lot, but we were shocked they had no non-smoking options (did anyone else hear otherwise?).Pay for internet access?? Please. US$6 per hour, not a lot, but was it really necessary at an all inclusive resort?Again, the disco was not what we thought. Now, other reviews have said that Punta Cana resorts don't have good discos in general. Believe it, it's true. We were hoping for salsa and merengue but got reggaeton and American Pop instead and the small room was filled with mostly teens and college students.Bring everything you need, because the prices for amenities in the little shops are unbelievable. A tiny 4oz bottle of suntan lotion was RD$525 or about US$17 and that was the cheapest and smallest. Postcards were a dollar.One thing my wife noticed was that there were mostly women at LTI, so dancing in the disco or with the live band was not easy unless women danced with women. The male:female ratio was not all balanced. There were definitely tons of single women but few single men - so maybe that is actually a plus for some of you! All in all, having never been to Punta Cana, nor an all inclusive resort, it was a lovely experience and very, very, very relaxing. We had so much time on our hands at first we didn鈥檛 know what to do with ourselves. By the second day we got the hang of it and started to just RELAX, know and accept that we didn鈥檛 have to do ANYTHING unless we wanted to. Now that鈥檚 a vacation ! We would recommend LTI to friends, especially those with children, but we also think that if we returned to Punta Cana (which we might) we would want to try another resort to see what else is out there !

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Enjoyed LTI We returned from LTI last week and want to add some positive feedback. Some of the recent reviews have covered most of the details so we will not duplicate what they have said. This is a beautiful, clean resort with generally very friendly people. (One desk clerk was an exception.) We, also, left a few dollars daily in tips and received excellent service in return. The servers remember who the tippers are. We found the food to be better than other reviews have indicated and we enjoyed the diversity and choices of the main buffet. We didn't like everything, but there were choices. (The dark chocolate ice cream is to die for, but unfortunately it wasn't available every day.) We tried the seafood restaurant but were generally happy with the buffet or the barbecue by the pool. What we wish we had known: More Spanish would have been very helpful and appreciated by the employees. They try hard to communicate in English but we felt that we should have known a bit more of their language. Also, if you want good snorkeling you may be disappointed. The trip we took had more snorkelers than fish, and most people had never gone snorkeling before. It was really just a very loud party. I think it was called Caribbean Festival and we wouldn't recommend it. We also went on the Outback Safari which we would highly recommend. It was a great way to learn a bit more about the country we are visiting. Just remember that with all these trips they seem to cram way too many people into a small space. And yes, some of the other tourists can be quite rude but don't let that ruin your vacation. We just tried to be unfailingly courteous and polite and to do our part to make Americans look better than might be expected based on our reputation abroad. We were aware that LTI is frequented by Europeans and that Speedos and topless sunbathing are the norm, but this can still be a bit off-putting for many Americans. So enjoy LTI. Perhaps we will see you there next year! Buen viaje!.

<Author>CRUSHADAVE
<Content>Beautiful resort My wife and I just returned from the LTI in Punta Cana. After reading some of the reviews, we were a little nervous about what to expect, but soon found it to be a great place for a vacation. Let me preface this by saying that we have been to 6 other all-inclusives throughout the Carribean, so we are very familiar with the way they work. we usually stay at a 3/4 star similar to this. I tend to be long winded, but here it goes...... THE BEACH: 10/10The beach here was the most beautiful we have seen! The softest sand, and beautiful water. There is a reef about 1/2 mile out or so where the waves break. Those whitecaps really make it a wonderful sight.THE RESORT: 8/10The resort itself was great. It is a fairly small resort, with a great layout. Meaning you can walk from the lobby to the beach within 5 minutes. All the restuarants are centrally located by the pool and the beach. My wife and I enjoy these smaller resorts; we don't want to spend all of our time walking to the bar, restaurant, bathroom....etc. The rooms were fine, not fantastic, but very nice. The mattress is as hard as a rock, but just like most other resorts we have stayed. The buildings and the grounds are very well maintained. We thought it was very clean, with great looking grounds. THE POOL: 9/10We absolutely loved the pool. It was large enough to have its own kids area, volleyball area, polo area, and still have plenty of room for you to just swim or relax. Also there were plenty of stairs on all sides. There is a hot tub, but it is the same temperature as the pool, just with some air jets. Still nice for relaxing.THE STAFF: 10/10We thought the staff was great. They were always very nice and accomodating. We always tend to make friends the first day or so, and recieve FABULOUS SERVICE the rest of the week. The average Dominican only makes $200-250 a month!! They all work 6 days a week; so if you find someone you like they will be there almost everyday. I suggest throwing them a five the first day, and you will get the best service. We did this at each bar and restaurant, and they never forgot us the whole week. I tend to over tip at home so I did the same here. Always left a few bucks for breakfast($3) and dinner($5), and found it to be well worth it. You will always be greeted with Hola mi amigo, and not have to ask for a thing! One night we got a special bottle of wine from one of the bartenders, and our glasses were always full. All the bartenders and waitstaff speak English, but the maids do not. THE FOOD: 6/10This is the one downfall of the LTI. Not that the food is bad. I do not want to scare off anyone from going. Breakfast is the best meal. (hard to mess that up!! lol) There are well over 30 different items including eggs, crepes, pancakes, omelets, hot/cold cereals, plenty of fresh fruit, along with specialty Dominican dishes. My wife and I really loved the fresh pineapple, sausauge, fruit shakes, bacon, and homemade donuts that tasted like fried dough! We also found the coffee to be very good, but strong.Lunch also had a buffet, a pizza restaurant, and food by the pool. We generally ate by the pool or grabed a slice of pizza. The pizza is VERY good. Thin crust, a little greasy, but tasty. There are 4 or 5 kinds buffet style including plain, pepperoni, onion, mushroom, etc. By the pool, there are burgers (ok), hot dogs(yuk), good french fries and chicken. We loved the chicken, it had a very good tasting spice on it. There also was a small buffet by the pool with a rice, veggie, pasta dish, great olives, and desserts. It was pretty good.Dinner good have been much better. There is a buffet at the main restaurant, with plenty of different items. I tend to try everything, and found most of the meats to be tough, and all the veggies cooked the same way, soaked in butter. No matter what veggie I had, it was cooked the same way. But there were plenty of options here, and even the pickiest eater should be able to find something. There also was a smaller buffet by the pool, just like lunch. There are 2 alcarte places. Generally when we have been away, these restuarants had the best food, but not here. One is Itailian, but is actually the same pizza place as lunch. They offer the pizza and a small buffet of pasta items. I wanted a good meal for dinner, not pizza. I suggest going for lunch, it is the same thing and you don't have to dress up. The other a seafood resturuant is hit or miss. You have your choice of four entrees. One chicken, one pork, one lamb/veal, one fish. The have other choices that you can pay extra for. We payed extra for the prawns appetizer($6), and would highly recommend it. A couple we met for dinner tried the filet and sirlion at extra charges (about $10 each), but did not find it very good(tough). The food here is OK, but the menu is the same everynight. (it changes on Mondays), so after 2 nights there, you've tried everything. THE DRINKS:I drink mostly beer. El Presidente was fine, like a light beer. You'll find it much colder and tastier at El Bucanaro (pool) and at the pizza place. It always tasted funny at the bar by the stage and was warm at the beach bar. My wife found the wine not to be so good. Once we made friends we got the better stuff, but still was just ok. Mixed drinks were very strong. They have house rum and good rum if you ask. (or tip them or it) DRESS:The seafood restaurant is the dressiest. I wore long pants there, but went to shorts at night for all others. They don't bother you. Most places we've been had 3 or 4 fancy restaurants, and you had to were long pants; not here. Why wear long pants to a pizza place or a buffet?? I just put on a nice shirt, dress shorts and she wore slacks and a sexy shirt. :) Just like if we went to dinner at home. CAYENNA BEACH CLUB:This is a small separate club next door. It was very tiny, with a VERY tiny pool of its own. I would not spend the extra money to stay there unless you wanted total privacy. It has one bar/restaurant of its own, but you have to go to the LTI for everything else. There are people at the LTI whose job it is to try to get to to go over to the Cayenna. They are trying to sell you a timeshare; and can be very annoying!! I had to threaten to throw one of them in the pool before they left us alone!! :)ENTERTAINMENT: 7/10The entertainment was ok. It is a good way to wind down after dinner, but don't expect too much. The shows consist of 2 local dance shows, a kareoki night, comedy night....the local dances were interesting and the girls all wore thongs....lolThey have waitress service at the shows which was a first for us. Also there are some jewlery vendors on 2 nights. They will pester you to buy. We did buy, but for about a tenth of what they were asking. Just start to walk away, they will lower the price.ACTIVITIES: 9/10We chose not to do much but relax. With 4 kids here at home, we needed it. Most activities were down on the beach. They had games, volleyball, soccer, boche, water polo, aerobics, ping pong.....whatever you want. The best thing is they were not pushy to get you involved. Relax if you want, play if you want. You can also snorkel, sail, parasail, kayak. Just no Jetskis, not sure why???WHAT TO BRING:We were well prepared after reading reviews on here. Plenty of sunscreen and solarcane! You do not want to have to buy it there. We brought 5 kinds, and gradually got more sun each day. It is VERY strong! One couple we met got fried and had to buy solarcane for about $20.Don't over pack dress clothes; just dressy casual. I did get sick one day; glad I had that Immodium!! There were no bugs, but we did bring spray. We brought $50 in ones and $100 in fives. Used it for tips as well as for smaller items so we would not have to get pesos for change. Bring something the size of a credit card. It'll keep your ac on all day. I actually used the stubs from our boarding passes! (like Mcgyver) The best thing we brought were those insulated mugs. I bought 2 of them at the dollar store before we left. They held 15oz (instead of the 7ozg cups), and kept everything cold as well as kept the sand out.Brush up on your Spanish. My 5 years in high school really helped, and they like it when you try to talk to them in their language, even if its broken.Oh and for you New England people, they absolutely love the Sox!! Wear a hat, shirt, anything and they will just start talking to you about Papi, Manny, and Pedro. If you can get some cheap hats, I'd bring those as tips! They will go a long way.WEATHER:Sunny, sunny, sunny, 85 everyday with a nice breeze. Very similar to Aruba. Absolutely beautiful. If it rained, it rained hard for about 5-10 minutes, then cleared up.OTHER GUESTS:There are very few english speaking guests, maybe 10%. Mostly from Germany and Italy. The only annoying thing we found is that when they are walking down the sidewalk, they walk down the middle and expect you to move, instead of going to the right(or even the left). Must be a Europe thing. ??? OVERVIEW:We loved the LTI. The beach and the layout of the resort was perfect for us. The food was good for breakfast and lunch, but dinner could have been better. The good new is that that can change. I'd like to see them change the Italian (pizza) restaurant to something else, and improve the food at the seafood restaurant. If they could do that, LTI would be perfect for us! We would definitely go back anyway. Actually looking to take the kids this November.......Well we hope this helps. Relax, enjoy, don't expect gourmet meals and you will love it!!Feel free to email me if you have questions. Just put LTI in the subject so I know its not spam. :)CRUSHADAVE

<Author>newhamsphireof4
<Content>Just loved the LTI Beach Resort My husband and I stayed at the LTI from January 27 to February 3 and must say we had a fabulous time and loved the resort and all it had to offer. I can't believe some of the reviews I had read about how bad it was, it seems as though we were at different resorts, I sure am glad that we did stay there. We arrived late because our plane left Boston later but we were on our way to the resort in no time and upon arriving at the LTI we were greeted by friendly and smiling bellboys along with a young lady offering us a nice fruit punch. The lobby was just beautiful with the floors that shined like a mirror, beautiful flowers, couches, tables and chairs and a bar. Check in was fast as it was around 8:30pm so we were off to our rooms immediately and to the buffet before it closed at 9:30. The rooms were immaculate and very spacious with a king size bed, two closets, a good size bathroom and a balcony with two chairs and a small table along with a small clothes line for wet clothes. Also a refrigerator with 2 pepsi's, 2 7-up's and two large containers of bottled water. The bathroom had soap dispensers by the sink and in the shower/tub, I brought my own face cloths as they don't have them. The resort was very well layed out with all the rooms on one side with building 1 through 5, 5 being nearest to the beach. The El Mirador Restaurant is the buffet, serving breakfast, lunch and dinner and on some nights having theme nights, which had 3 seperate sections to eat in, non-smoking, smoking and half and half which was great. The variety of food there was awesome, always something different and if you went hungry it was your own fault. The desserts, ice cream and breads were so good. Casual dress there, you could wear your bathing suit but it had to be covered. The El Bucanero restaurant was by the beach and had BBQ everyday along with other food, there you could go in barefoot and bathing suit, again variety good. This place was open 24 hours a day. The La Trattoria restaurant was Italian with pizza along with a buffet of different items. You need reservations for this place along with the Estrella del Mar which we did not eat at. The pool was very very large and very well kept with plenty of room, it was very refreshing when it was 86 and no breeze. The beach of course was just beautiful and a very large beach with plenty of chairs and very clean. The entertainment at night really fun. The young people that work during the day playing games and keeping people occupied were awesome and would be part of the show at night so we saw them working more than 12 hour days. The waiters were always smiling and if they remembered you your coffee or drink would be at your table when you returned with your food. There a few bulletinboards around which list what is going on so that was nice to know and how to plan accordingly. Nice shops and twice during the week they have natives that come and sell their wooden carvings, jewelry and paintings. Also, there are huts down the beach that sell everything you can imgaine so you can go and deal with them also. All are so friendly. Again this resort was very very clean, the ground were very well maintained as was everything, fun, relaxing and would definetely stay there again in a heartbeat. I could just go on and on but sure you get my point about this resort. Any questions please fell free to ask.

<Content>An honest opinion of LTI/Cayena I had many concerns due to items that I read on this site and here is my review.RoomsI stayed at the Cayena Beach Club portion of LTI and it seemed to definitely be nicer than the basic LTI. The rooms are bigger and closer to the beach but the basic rooms are accommodating. You get what you pay for and remember that you are not in the US and things are going to be tougher if you don't speak the language. Leave the workers a couple of bucks every day or every other day and they will appreciate it and may give you extra service. The people there are all nice and friendly and if you don't speak Spanish be patient.FOODThe Cayena offers a separate restaurant, which allows you to have food special, ordered which is nice if you're not a big fan of buffets. The rest of the options are buffet type and the food is not outstanding but it's OK. All have different hours and menus and some require reservations so when you get there ask for the times and requirements otherwise you may not be able to dine there that night. My girlfriend and I ate everything that was hot and we never had any issues with food. I believe after talking to people who got sick they all did the same two things 1. Drank the water or 2. Ate or drank on an excursion off the resort. Only eat at the resort and drink the bottled water they provide and you should be fine. DRINKSGood and strong- sometimes a little too strong so tell them to stop otherwise they will give you an entire glass full of rum with a dash of coke. Draft beer only--It's called Presidente and its not bad. When they wash the glasses it's in treated water so don't worry if they wash out your glass. AtmosphereIt's a great place if you want to relax, drink and lay in the sun. The beach along with the pools are super nice. They have a show at night that's like a high school variety show or ultra low budget Vegas show depending on the night. It's worth a couple of laughs. The disco is nothing other than the people from the show trying to get others to dance and have a good time. Unless you're beyond drunk and with a bunch of people, I can't imagine having much fun there. Also, if you're single and looking to hook up, this resort is not the place to go. I saw about maximum 3 or 4 single guys/girls there that looked single and they might not have even been single.A great place to go with spouse or girlfriend though as long as you both like to sun and drink. They have a casino close by that that's about ten tables-unless you're desperate to play BJ or craps it's not worth it. OverallI would go back to LTI for the money if you can get a cheap flight to DR I would recommend it. If you have any additional questions- email me at Fneedles_2000@yahoo.com.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>LTI Beach Resort - a great place to relax My friend and I spent a relaxing, fully enjoyable week at the LTI Beach Resort from Dec. 31 through Jan. 8th. After reading several negative reports about this hotel, we arrived, a bit apprehensive about what we might expect. I have only one question to ask the nay-sayers. What hotel did you stay in? The LTI is a wonderful resort with excellent, friendly staff, beautiful grounds, exquisite beach and very nice rooms. The food was varied and well prepared. The buffet was huge! The Italian restaurant was great - lots of variety in pizza and always a speciality pasta dish and several varieties of lasagne along with the salad and antipasto bar. The Bucaneer was great for lunch as it was very informal and right on the beach. Also handy to pick up ice and ice water. New Years Eve was special with all of the decorations and the added zest for that special holiday. Although we were dead tired from our very early morning flight, we had a great dinner and felt that the resort went to a lot of work to put on a super evening. We were concerned about the supposed rules for attire, but we found out that as long as you were tasteful, there was no problem. New Years Eve tended to be dressy, but for the most part, dress shorts, slacks, capri pants, skirts and nice sandals were worn by most guests at the buffet. Most gentlemen wore long trousers for dinner. Who can blame the hotel for wanting bathingsuits covered up and something a little more elegant than flip flops in their dinning room? Common sense is the best course of action. We were delighted by the large number of huts available at the beach. As a habitual early riser, I never had a problem getting my favourite location under a hut by 7 a.m. There always seemed to be availability. Some complain about towel insufficiencies - never had a problem getting a towel. Of course, if you wanted to change towels several times a day, then, perhaps you found a shortage as the hotel has to have time to launder the towels. Shopping on the beach was quite an experience and bartering is the expected. We were approached once by the yellow shirted time-share gurus. When firmly told no, they did not argue or pursue discussion. Our maid was very helpful - the pillows are thin, but all we had to do was ask for a second pillow and it was provided promptly. We received flowers in our room several times over the week and our fridge was kept well stocked with water and sodas. If you want your toilet to work well, cut down on the quantity of paper you feed it. Same rules you would use with a septic system. Above all, when travelling to a foreign country, leave your biases at home. All countries are different. Appreciate the natural beauty of the geography, the culture of the people and the bounty afforded by new experiences. Accept the fact that home is home and travel is travel. If you want it just like home, then stay at home. I'd return to the LTI Beach Resort in a heartbeat - loved it.
