<Content>2005-2006 review Date: Jan 3rd 2006We were my wife and I, my 14 month son and the 2 parents of my wife on a limited budget.We are writing this comments as we are still staying in the Hotel. Here is our feedback after 2 weeks:Hotel population: 40% German. 30% Italian, 15% French Europe/Canada , 10% English Canadian/US, 5% misc. What is good:- Small hotel (only 450 rooms) therefore a bit more personal.- The food is good, knowing that it's all-inclusive, breakfast are usually the same every morning at the Mirador, but you can vary what you eat due to the choice of dishes. Food at the Hestrela del mar is excellent. European touch cooking. - The swimming pool is HUGE !! 3 in total.- Nice people working there, The Animacion people are nice and good with the kids, but lazy sometimes.- They are expanding to include a golf course in their list of activities.- Silent air conditioning and fan in the room. Helps when you want to sleep!- Every day refill of your fridge with pops and water.What is bad:- Lots of problems in the rooms, air conditioning licking, old and broken bathroom appliances, Toilette flushing not always working properly, TV not working, defective electrical outlets, only one very flat pillow per bed and no additional in the room. The rooms need definitely a good refresh!- Don't supply face/washcloths. Bring them if you need.- Swimming pool area for kids (the 30cm area), the bottom of the pool's concrete is peeling off and can be dangerous for babies' feet.- After 1 pm, it's very hard to find a clean dry towel at the swimming pool, they are always out of stock.- Said in the ad that they had a spa. It's not even built yet!! The Spa section is some bear brick walls hidden by wooden boards. I guess it will be finish in 2 to 3 months or so.- The beach is still the Atlantic sea therefore you have waves, seaweeds and a swimming distance away from the shore of about 150 ft only. Then you cross the buoys and you are in the powerboat path! And there are crazy! But it is not too bad after all. The hotel is right on the beach and the quality of the sand is remarkable comparing to some of the other hotels on the island. - Useless personnel at the guest service. They dont know the answer of half of your questions and suggest only the places they get a commission from... I guess...- The worst of all, we saw cockroaches crawling on the floor in the main restaurant during the dinner. We went to talk to the General Manager on the hotel and said, in a very impolite way, that was impossible and waked away!...prick...! The problem is not the little cute bugs but THE MANAGER!Punta Cana  surrondings52 Hotels side by side, nothing to visit unless you go outside of the hotel area.Bavaro market, $6.00 away by taxi and we found a market of about 200 little stores selling exactly the same things with on commission locals who are over soliciting you to buy something in their store. By the way, you can barging up to 70% of the asking price!! Don't be fooled!!Tricks  Tips- If you are interested in this hotel, check first the VIP section called the Cayena beach club, you can get a way better service that the hotel. Try to talk to Gilles, client manager of the Cayena.- Go to the beach market instead of the Bavaro complex, they are nicer people and the prices are the same.- Best rooms are in the block 5 from room 5115 to 5129 or 5215 to 5229 facing the ocean.- insert a old phone card in the electric auto shut-off located next to the door in order to keep your electricy in the room running. Good when you charge your laptop or want to kep the room chill with the A/C.- Don't drink to much Pina Collada, it's a laxative! ouch..- Don't take the lobsters from their loster night, they are tasteless, overcooked and expensive.- If you rent a car, watch the road they are full of BIG holes, specialy next to new construction area.Bottom line, ok hotel for smaller budget. Great hotel if you have kids.

<Content>Surprisingly good! Just returned from LTI Punta Cana. We were happily surprised at this resort. We had a bad experience last year at Bavaro Beach Resort which was horrible. We found LTI to be very professionaly run  every inch of the property to be immaculate. Staff was helpful and friendly w/out going overboard which can be annoying. Grounds are lovely; beach is gorgeous w/plenty of chairs  palapalas for all. The resort is layed out in a manner that allows easy access to everything w/out walking long distances. I would caution people w/small children that the water is very rough  I didn't see any children in the water for the week we were there. However the pool was huge w/plenty of places for children to play. The food was ok but we didn't expect gourmet anyway. You will never go hungry since there are plenty of choices. We ate lunch at the beach bar everyday  the grilled chicken was great. Rooms were more than adequate and cleaned thoroughly everyday. This resort is very quiet which is exactly what we wanted. For those looking for a lot of excitement, noise, etc this would not be a good choice. But for a relaxing week on a gorgeous beach, the LTI was a good choice for us. The bottom line: we would return.

<Content>Had a good time My boyfriend and ILTI and had a great time. Wasn't sure what to expect after reading some negative reviews and some positive reviews. It rained off and on 4 of the 7 nights which I didn't care as long as it didn't rain during the day. Here are some basics of the hotelRoom: has 2 twin beds pushed together to make king. I slept great every night. A nice balcony with table and 2 chairs and line to hang up towels, bathing suits, etc., tv only gets about 5 channels in english, you need to get a remote from the front desk. We rented the safe for $2/day ( well worth it) Bathroom very nice with big mirror and marble shower. No irons, bring your own.Food: I am NOT a picky eater and even I complained about the food (to my boyfriend of course) The Italian Restaurant was yuck. I learned fast I didn't like the Dominican cheese. El Mirador is the best for breakfast and supper since they offer the biggest selection of food. Lunch I recommend El Bucanero since it is the only restaurant you can go in with bare feet and bathing suits and also it is right next to the grill that has Hamburgs, hotdogs (not american) chicken and french fries. Some of the food you just have to risk trying. The desserts are excellent. Drinks: I only had 2 alcohol beverages during my stay. The Banana Mama and Pina Colada. They are excellent! My boyfriend only drank Presidente's and Black Rum and Pepsi's. Beach/Pool: Beach and Pool are the most beautiful I've ever seen. Beach has some seaweed, but softest sand I've ever felt. Don't bother looking for seashells there are none! There were days when we didn't get to the beach until 10 am and there were still plenty of lounge chairs available. I have medium pale skin and I wore spf 50 and still got a good tan. Be sure to bring your own sunscreen, it is $27 in hotel shops.Entertainment: The activities crew works very hard to make people have a good time. We participated in beach baseball, salsa dancing, meringue dancing, yoga,pilates, and volleyball. It was really fun! If you win a contest you win a free bottle of rum at the show at nightime. We didn't leave the resort except for walks along the beach. Also went wind sailing which I recommend..really nice. Only non-motorized water sports available with all-inclusive. Hotel did offer Banana-boat rides (which looked like a lot of fun) for $5 I think. Shows at night were great. The activities crew work every day all day and all night from 9a-12a. Two of them even got married on the beach during our stay :) and still had to come back to work during night. They are very fun, young, nice people. Shopping: There are shops located on the beach if you walk towards your left down the beach around the corner. Good place to buy souvenirs but beware of there offering prices. You have to bargain. Our representative told us to offer 60% less than what they ask for....they ask for ridiculous prices becvause they think all americans are rich. no need to exchange your american money. Bring small bills for shopping.Overall: I don't think I'd go back to LTI just because there are so many more places I'd like to visit. But......in 20 years if I decide to go back to Punta Cana I would go back to LTI.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A wonderful week We stayed in the Cayena section of the LTI resort and our room was amazing. Beachfront view from our patio, comfortable beds, crisp air conditioning, and my favorite was the lovely marble bathroom. I found the window on the door and the shutters that opened to the room charming and the tub alone was almost the size of my whole NYC bathroom. I would have liked a few more bottles of water in the fridge each day, but asking for a couple extra when passing the bar was minor.GROUNDS - Were well-kept and clean although simple in design compared to some other resorts (we walked through plenty of other resorts to check it out). It's not as new as some of the hotels more north on the beach, nor as grand as the Princess hotels grounds, but they keep up well the repair and grooming. In fact, we both said this looks like Orlando to some of the newer, more American-populated hotels. I appreciated the un-Florida-ness of the LTA grounds. The LTI lounge chairs were newer and more comfy than many other hotels. We were able to get the same spot on the beach every day even if we didn't get our towels out until 9:30 or 10.PEOPLE - It is a German owned resort so a majority of the guests in the LTI section are German or French. The Cayena section was predominantly American and according to the staff usually is. We interacted more with the staff and people we met in town than other tourists, though. I speak a little Spanish and my boyfriend is a native Spanish speaker so we did not experience the same barrier many speak of. However, it bothered me to see a few people speaking to the staff in forceful German or English as if the staff was stupid for not being fluent. They are all bilingual to varying degrees but they are working class people from a Spanish-speaking country! We are in their country. A little bit of effort goes miles toward a week of pleasant interactions. The bartenders and waitstaff in both the Cayena section and main buffet restaurants were so friendly we even got a couple mini-parties on the last day. The timeshare guys on the beach can be pushy but they speak 3 or 4 languages so are the easiest to have a conversation with (and therefore get them to chill out on asking you to come see their presentation).WEATHER - We arrived just after a week of rainy weather and Hurricane Wilma passed south and west of us, so it was perfect all week. Sunny every day with a few brief tropical showers.FOOD - Liked it. I am a certified NY restaurant snob and I had resigned myself to a week of turkey sandwiches but was pleasantly surprised. Eating lunch in the Cayena section restaurant was a big plus because the lunches seemed to be the weakest in the LTI restaurants, but in the Cayena restaurant you can get duck, scallops, or a cubano sandwich. El Bucanero always had dependable chicken (moist and perfectly grill-kissed), ribs, baked potatoes, and hot dogs. The buffet restaurant had different themes each night and while the Chinese night was perhaps questionable the Dominican night and Seafood night were excellent with local dishes, produce, and catches. Whole suckling pig? Shrimp that was just pulled out of the ocean? Desserts made with Dominican sugar cane? Yum. We also went to the Langosta del Caribe restaurant off-site for lunch one day and it put New England style lobster to shame. The rest of the meal was eh and touristy but the lobster itself... muy rica. The LTI specialty restaurants were only OK and not worth the effort to make reservations. The drinks were pretty good. Sometimes too strong, once or twice a little smooth, but you can ask the bartender to make it with less alcohol. The boyfriend loved the Mamajuana so much he asked 3 bartenders to whip up their own version for us to take home. Fresh local fruit was available always.If you have an adventurous streak, walk to the road from one of the little tourist shop areas and flag down a guy with a moped. Whether buzzing around more rural roads or going past the Plaza Bavaro into the town area of Bavaro, it feels more like a foreign country. You can also go dancing with a better variety of people and music AND find souvenirs to take home for 1/4 the price as near the resorts. Parasailing = worth the price charged. Horseback riding = while the lengthier sunset ride looked like a great time, the prices were the same as taking a longer ride in Hawaii which made no sense.We will be going back next year.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Family fun in paradise We just returned from LTI and I must say it was much more than I expected especially after some of the bad reviews I read before we left. The hotel grounds are a bit older and smaller than most, but they make up for it with very pretty trees, flowers, and beach front. As most said, you need to get up early to find a covered spot at the beach, but no one bothers anything after you leave your towels. The sun is hotter than anything you experience in the states and 30 to 50 spf has little effect on it. Our whole family went (two boys and two girls all 14 to 24) and there was plenty to do and plenty to eat and drink. You could walk the beach, kyack, snorkel, but windsurfing for our teenage boys was a hassle because they wanted to sell them lessons.... The vendors on the beach were the cheapest buys we found anywhere after a bit of negotiation. Rum, coffee, and vanilla all go for about the same price unless you a buying in bulk.We took a few rolls from the buffet when we snorkled and it produced awesome results. The snorkling area is small, but you can still see a lot.The rooms were nice, the service was great, and our Vacation Express rep was very helpful. We took the Jurassic Expedition inland and it was awesome. We brought bags of candy bars, pencils, toothbrushes, and other goodies to give to the children as we traveled along. It was definitely worth the $78 per person. The airport was a bit confusing and there wasn't much help available. The bus into and out of the hotel was great. My wife and I worried some about the toplessness on the beach, and there was plenty, but it was never a problem.We did an All-Inclusive at Breezes in Jamaica 10 years ago and this was acutually a better bang for the buck. Like any vacation, there were a few glitches, but overall this was a great trip. We were all part of a very cultural experience and it has changed the way we think of the world.

I was very happy we didn't take our son. I don't have issues with it if that's what you like, but it's not what I would have wanted for my 7 yr. old son to experience. All in all, had a wonderful time and I think everyone should experience it but you definitely have to have an open mind.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great family getaway Just back after 2 weeks at the LTI. Had a great first vacation in the DR. Left Edmonton after a spring snowfall of 6 inches and -21 to +34 in one day! Our flight ,Air Transat arrived with an Air France flight so the line was huge going through customs approx 1/2 hr. Have tourist card filled out BEFORE you get there. A passport is better than birth certificates and drivers licences as this held up the line. Check tour company signs for bus number then proceed to the parking lot to find it. No need to take any adventerous excursions as the bus ride to the hotel fit this bill. If you arrive at night 1030 pm as we did the reception went extremely quick with only a handfull of guests. Our rooms were in the first building #s 1205 and 07, 1 for Mom and Dad the other for our two teens. Rooms were clean use a plastic card ie zellers point card to keep air conditioning and electricity working when you take your key. No bugs or mozzies but discovered the worlds largest cockroach before my wife had the shower, place a towel by the front door to prevent unwanted creatures. The shower only dribbled out and you loose pressure at peak times ie morning and just before dinner. Tipped the maid a buck or two to ensure she would clean our rooms in the morning vice 5pm. You only get a 7up and a pepsi along with a 4lt jug of water. No problems finding variety of food at ala cartes or buffets you could survive on just the deserts. Keep your beach towels at the end of the day to place them on a lounge chair at 6am or your out of luck. We went to relax and get a sun tan and we certainly achieved that. Don't swim with the dolphins as it is 95US for two minutes and a picture, we were warned and did not contribute to the animals plight same with the horse back riding, we went as horse owners and found the animals overworked, poor tack and as fun as the safeway horse ride. The ride will cost you 50US per pers for two hrs at 4 - 6 pm on a beach bring jeans and be prepared to get a bit dirty. We had no problems with the staff a little spanish helps. Say mucho ron to get a stiffer drink, tip and use the same bartender for great service. The beach venders are left up the beach we could usually bring them down 50% as they over priced the items anyway ALL cigars are cheap imitations for those so inclined better price at the airport duty free when leaving. Check out at noon means your sitting around the lobby until you leave for the airport 6 1/2 hrs for us. Have 20US for departure tax. The same for having your luggage overweight you have to pay cash in US or DR peso. Using travellers checks is fine at the hotel as you can get US in change. Only one case of GI (me) for one day bring Imodium. We definitely would recommend staying at this hotel for a budget oriented stay.

<Author>missey81
<Content>Had a great vacation, but........ After reading all the reviews about LTI, I was a little nervous about going.We did have a great time, but some of the reviews were correct. #1 VERY IMPORTANT: My husband and I, my very good friend and her husband, and my brother stayed at the Cayena, which is a small resort off the LTI Beach Club. There are only 47 rooms in the resort compared to 447 at LTI. It is an upgrade from LTI that is run by Interval International. When I booked three rooms from Interval, one for us, one for my friend and one for my brother, no one explained double occupancy. The average traveler might think that double occupancy applied to the room and even if you were one person, your were paying the same price for the room, OK no problem. However, NO ONE bothered to explain that double occupancy meant double all inclusive. Yes thats right... he had to pay for 2 all inclusive meal plans. So instead of paying $460.00 he had to pay $980.00. We have been to resorts in Santa Domingo, and La Romana, and this was the first time that this happened. SOOOOO.... be sure to read all the FINE print. It was on the confirmation, the very end of the confirmation, so we lost the battle. If you are traveling solo....be sure to check!From what I saw at the LTI, it was primarily German and French. The Germans are very rude, but if you don't let them bother you, you won't have a problem. Cayena is primarily American families. The food at LTI was o.k. at the main dinning area. We had one meal that was not so good, very salty, but not bad. Breakfast and Lunch we had at Cayena, and it was OUTSTANDING! According to people who work there, dinner hours were starting April 10th, so if you are staying at Cayena, there will be no need to go to LTI. The seafood rest. at LTI was good, but we paid extra for the steak and lobster. It was worth it. Did not make it to other areas, but heard Italian was good, and EL Bucanero (not sure of spelling) was good. Out of our group of 5, 4 of us got sick. My husband was the worst with vomiting and diarrhea. We had been taking Cipro as a precaution, but he still got sick. I was told that it was due to a type of irritable bowel syndrome due to eating food without preservatives. Because our bodies are not use to it, it takes time to adjust. Not sure, did not last more than a day, BE SURE TO TAKE IMMODIUM WITH YOU. The beach was OUTSTANDING! There are many huts with chairs, but if you want a prime spot, get up by 6:00 and put your towels out. No one touched them, so if you were worried about other peoples thoughts on the subject, don't be. The weather was great also. Sun is very warm, so be sure to pack the 45 sun block.Rooms were ok at Cayena. They were a little bigger that the normal room; small sitting area, and bedroom with 2 double beds. Nothing spectacular. I really did expect more, but who stays in the room when on vacation.......not me!Not much to do at night, but you can walk to other resorts or take a cab to where ever you want to go. After being in the sun all day, we really did not want to go out at night. Did not see any mosq., and no one talked about malaria. My friends husband did have bites of some sort on his hand, not sure from what. He stayed more at the pool than the beach, so just not sure!All in all we had a really good trip. Vacations are what you make them. Would I go back to that resort....no. Would like to see other places. But if you are going, I am sure you will have a good time. If you can upgrade to Cayena, it is worth it.Any questions, please feel free to e-mail me at henry8@rcn.com.hola chicos!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Time; family had fun; food so-so My wife, three sons and I just returned from a 7-day stay in Punta Cana at LTI. Overall, we had a really nice time with wonderful weather. Highlights for us were the pool and beach, while the food was only so-so.ROOMWe had a deluxe room since we were a group of 5. Our three boys (ages 10, 7, and 4) had a separate room with 2 beds and a pull-out couch. We had a king bed in the main room. We had a great view of the ocean from our balcony. They stocked the fridge with soda and bottled water only. FOODThis was far and away the weakest part of LTI. I overheard someone say everything here has a taste, and that's dead on. Everything, right down to the bottled soda, had a funky taste. The Pepsi tasted like it had ginger it, all the cakes tasted like rum was added. So, if you like to experiment, you'll get your chance, if not, you'll be fairly limited.Breakfast was good, with make-your-own omeletes, eggs, bacon, sausage, and donuts as the highlights. Also, the grill at the El Bucanero had good meats and fairly normal french fries.SERVICEEveryone had a great attitude. The Dominicans absolutely love kids. The maid did an adequate job, but was not exceptional. The servers at the restaurants were fairly lax, but got around to you eventually. Tipping helped, but you got someone different every day, so we didn't quite see the point.Our transfer arrangements to and from the airport were well organized (we used Transglobal Vacations).POOL/BEACHFor our family, this was the best part of LTI. The pool was wonderful - there were perfect shady spots for the young kids, and nets and basketball hoops for our oldest son. The water was always warm and was generally not that crowded, except over the weekend.The beach was absoultely gorgeous. The waves were manageable for all but the yougest kids. We didn't obsess about reserving chairs, and managed to find shady spots later in the day. If you're a major beach junkie, you should probably take others' advice and get there between 6:00 and 6:30 AM.MISCELLANEOUS POINTS- Our kids liked the kids club and Bea did a great job. Another family told us there were days when the other kids and teacher spoke limited English.- As other reviewers have noted, there are lots of Germans there. We just found it easier to bond with other English speaking people. So, we weren't bothered too much - other than guys in speedos everywhere (AHHHH!!!!!)- I had nasty stomach pains 2 of the 7 days I was there - not sure what caused it, but Immodium A-D helped. Everyone else was healthy.- We saw virtually no bugs.- Internet is available for around $6 US per hour. This was a great way to stay in touch.- We never left the resort, but another family told us the monster safari tour was really interesting.Overall, we really did have a great time. However, we probably wouldn't go back because of the limited food, and hesitation about leaving the resort with kids.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great beach getaway My girlfriends and I just returned from a beautiful 5 day vacation to Punta Cana. I was a little worried about going after reading some poor reviews but this trip was one of the best I have been on. We booked through Funjet Vacations out of Detroit. We arrived on time and were quickly shown to our bus to the hotel. Check in at the LTI was no problem. We did have to wait for our room about an hour, just enough time to check out the grounds and get some lunch. Our room was the building fartherest from the beach but with the most spectacular view of the grounds and ocean. We were able to sleep with our doorwall open everynight. The beach is beautiful. If you would like a lounge chair and a hut, I would suggest getting out there around 6:30 am to place towels on chairs. No one will bother them or move them. There are no clocks in the room so book a wake-up call then go back to sleep. As for nightlife, there is none on this resort. The disco at LTI opens at 11 pm and is pretty much cleared out by midnight. The last night there we were taken by cab ($6 US) to the Munga Disco located at another resort (I believe it was the Occidental resort). We arrived at 12:30 am and there was still a line to get in at 4 am when we left. It is $6 US to get in but that includes one drink. There are 2 levels (only the bottom one was open on this Monday night). They play great native and american music that gets everyone out there dancing. The food was wonderful. Even my friend who is a vegetarian found enough to eat without a problem. The grounds are beautiful. I would watch out for the bugs. I got a ton of bites (my 2 other friends got none) so I would suggest some bug spray especailly if you are on the beach at night. Have fun and enjoy. I would definetly return to the LTI.

<Author>blally
<Content>Good trip, Ok Hotel My girlfriend and I just got back from the D.R. after staying at LTI from March 20-24, 2005. Overall the hotel is about 3 stars. We had a very good time but the beach and weather had more to do with our good experience than did the hotel. This hotel (and most in the DR) is mostly European. I would guess that the hotel was 80-85% Europeans (approx. 60% German, 10% French) and 15-20% American/Canadian. This creates a very european atmosphere at the hotel, which was fine with us but may be a problem for some americans. Of special note: many europeans go topless at the beach. Here's the breakdown.Beach: 5 Stars-the beach has beautiful, soft, white sand and crystal clear water. The current is not very strong and it is very safe. The all inclusive package includes all non-motorized sports. I would encourage eveyone to take advantage of the free sailboats and kayaks. We paid to go snorkeling but didn't see many fish. *NOTE: the hotel has a bunch of cabanas but you need to get up EARLY in the morning to reserve them. Early means before 6:30. Rooms: 2 1/2 Stars-Our room was clean and had a nice view but other than that I was a little dissappointed. I have stayed at hotels all over the world and would not classify our room as anything more than average. Pushing two twins together to form a King is not my idea of luxury. That being said we didn't spend much time in our room and the room was otherwise adequate. Free bottle of water and pop in the fridge was nice. Grounds: 3 1/2 Stars-The ground were very well kept. They were clean, and pretty but not overally impressive.Staff: 3 Stars-The staff was satisfactory and nothing more. They didn't go out of there way to be helpful but they were not rude either. It appeared that there were several activities for children which would be nice if you have kids.Food: 2 Stars-The food was the biggest dissapointment of the trip. I tend to be a little critical of food, but my girlfriend and I agreed that the food was below average at best. Here is a breakdown of the food by restaurant. By the way: both of us got sick, which is odd for me. I have been to Mexico 7 times and never got sick so go figure.  Mirador: This is the main restuarant open for breakfast, lunch and dinner. While this restaurant had a variety of choice, many of them were not very good. The breakfast was satisfactory. I would stick with the croissants, bacon and cereal. The eggs and ommletes were good somedays and undercooked others. The fruit was ok. For dinner, I would suggest the pasta and bread. They had decent deserts. We did not have lunch here. No reservations needed. Snack Bar: The snack bar was disappointing. Yes, you can get a hamburger or hot dog at any time of the day but the burger was overcooked, on an oversized bun, and had no cheese. And no, cheese is not an option. The hotdog was equally bad.  Bucannero: We didn't eat here much since the food didn't look so great. Although you could make your own ham and cheese. The deserts were pretty decent. No reservations needed. Trattorio: Probably the best meal we had at the hotel was at the Trattorio. My pizza was different but good and the pasta was also pretty good. The desert again was good. Reservations needed. Note: You make the reservations the same day at the Mirador between 7:00 and 10:30 am. Seafood Restaurant: We opted for the all inclusive meals instead of the ala carte. The all inclusive dishes were very ok but not great. We purchased a good bottle of wine which was nice. Reservations needed.Bottom Line: I would not reccomend this hotel. If you get a great deal on it (like we did) you can roll with the punches and still have a great time. If you paid a lot of money you will probablly be dissapointed. If you are planning a trip check out the other options.Feel free to email mep.s. we paid a cab to take us to Santo Domingo (3 hours each way). While it cost 150 dollars I would highly recommend it to those who want to taste the culture of the Domincan. Driving through the country and exporing Santo Domingo was a highlight of our trip. I tend to be adventurous but would strongly advise NOT renting a car.

<Author>ajane
<Content>Great trip! My friend and I stayed at the LTI Beach Resort from Mar 6-10. We were both nervous about the place because there have been so many negative reviews. However, we ended up having a fantastic trip--only wish we could have stayed longer.I didn't have any problems with getting sick, although I came armed with Immodium. We mainly at at the grill for lunch and the buffet for lunch and dinner, both of which were fine. Breakfasts were probably the best at the buffet though--fresh fruit, omelettes/eggs made to order, breads. We did have dinner at the Italian restaurant--La Trattoria--which was okay, but nothing special. We chose to go back to the buffet for our last dinner because we liked having more options.The staff was incredibly friendly. True, those at reception during checking in and out were not the most congenial, but we only had to deal with them twice, so that didn't affect our trip at all. The cleaning people, groundskeepers, waiters, and bartenders were all charming and a little spanish goes a long way with them. The rooms are standard--nothing too special. We stayed in building 4 on the first floor and liked it. We didn't have a great view, but then we didn't come for a room with a view--we came for the beach! They were clean. We loved our cleaning lady--she brought us extra pop every day after we had requested it the first day. We did find one very large bug our first night, but that was the only bug we saw. I did have a problem with bug bites though. My friend didn't get bit at all and I had bites all over.Although we didn't really participate in the daily activities, we watched the nightly shows which were fun (not incredibly professional, but we loved them nonetheless). We also did go to the Club at night, which was tiny and few people attended. I had fun dancing with the animation staff--they really do a good job of getting you moving! I did leave the resort one night to go to Mangu, the club at Grand Flamenco, which I recommend if you are looking for a more hopping night life. It stays open very late, plays a wide variety of music, costs $6 US to get there via cab, and $6 US to get in. I had a blast there.All in all, for what I paid, this trip was a fabulous value. I would definitely stay at LTI again.

<Author>themarkel
<Content>March 2005 Trip Report Hotel is a good 40 minute drive from Punta Cana Airport, we flew in at night so could not see much along the way.The hotel has a large open lobby, marble floors and two out of six ceiling fans that actually work. Two gift shops ($35 for suntan lotion)and a cigar store are off the lobby.There are five buildings three floors each, of approx 40 rooms each, all have either a patio (1st floor) or balconies. Only building 5 has actual ocean views on one side. Most have views of the enormous pool and garden area.The main buffet restaurant serves breakast, lunch and dinner.Breakfast: This is the best of the three meals - made to order eggs and omlettes, European style pancakes (crepes), fresh fruits, pastries, numerous types of bread and rolls (excellent), cheeses, cold cuts, yogurts, cereals, bacon or ham, sausages, awesome potatoes!!, various milk shakes and more. A++ for breakfast.Lunch: Sometimes great pork ribs (not like those in the US though), but always a fish dish, salads of all kinds, cold cuts, rice, a pasta station, awesome desserts and more.Dinner: almost the same as lunch, but Turkey or beef or chicken, a pasta station not really much change from lunch. There are themes to each nights food but one would be hard pressed to differentiate them.There are two Specialty Restaurants that need reservations made at breakfast of the same day. You can eat there more than once. The Italian Restaurant is really just a Pizza Place with a small salad bar, a couple of pastas and deserts. there is even a surcharge for some of the Pizzas!!Best bet is to go here at lunch time - no reservation needed and various pizza by the slice offered.The Seafood Restaurant offers four entre choices, a fish, a pork chop, a chicken breast and veal slices - everything else - steaks, lobster etc have a high surcharge. Chicken and Pork chops were excellent. Slow service but good food.There is another buffet near the beach that offers a much smaller selection of the main buffet. There is also a BBQ shack attached that is open from 11am to about 6am. Burgers, hot dogs, chicken, sliced beef, sausage and grilled vegetables.There are bars all over the place - Main Buffet only offers beer (only Presedente - the local bear), wine and sodas. Drinks are more than strong enough and they just keep coming.The rooms are large tiled floors mainly with twin beds pushed together to make a king, color TV ( 20) HBO, Showtime, CNN and various sports networks and french, spanish and german stations. a small refridgerator (ours did not work well) with a gallon of bottled water and a Pepsi and 7up in it replaced as used, NO IRON  BOARD, bathroom has a dispenser for soap by the sink and shampoo in the tub, DO NOT DRINK THE WATER FROM THE FAUCET - YOU WILL GET SICK!!. The bathroom door has glass windows in the top half - different! also, no wash cloths offered.The beach is wonderful soft white sand with a slope into the water that is warm and even 20 feet out is not more than five foot deep, tons of huts to sit under, however by 6:30AM most all the prime ones have been taken with towels placed on them. Do not be shocked by the many topless women at the beach - very European.Watersports are offered with hour maximum daily on snorkelling and kayaks (singles and doubles), Hobie Cat has to be sailed by a member of their staff however. You can walk forever along the beach, to the left about 10 minutes are about 20 stalls at a flea market prices are absurd even when they expect you to bargain down 25 - 33% of the asking price. $25 for a Tee shirt at best you can get it down to maybe $10. For the more adventurous you can walk to the right about 40 minutes to TOWN but again prices are very high with few exceptions - coffee $3, local cheap rum $8 for a litre otherwise same ridiculous prices. Lots of women offering $10 massages.There is nightly entertainment put on by the Animation Team very funny worth a giggle you need to drink heavily to appreciate this though. These same guys and girls work all day long getting guests to participate in everything from arobics to volleyball.There is a very small disco open from 11pm to 2am but we never went and from what we heard from others neither did too many other people.Buy a handpainted Tee shirt from the gentleman at the pool $12 - $14 a true peice of art!We took a tour with Jurassic Safari an all day tour that leaves at 8:30am and returned around 6:30pm. You get to see the country to say the least. The people live in absolute poverty most do not have electricity or running water. Women collect water from dirt puddles and wash their clothes along the river. Children rush out to the street for you to throw them candy or when stopped to ask you for a dollar. They bring you to a Gift shop/Cigar store (very expensive), a typical Dominican House, lunch on a ranch (very good food) through a very small zoo with photo ops with a monkey, parrot, tarantula and snake, a walk across a cable bridge, a dip in the river, then off to a stall to buy rum - good prices, then through a sugar cane field and to the beach to boogie board. Alot of fun, alot of driving though. Our tour guide REGO was the most knowledgeable guide with answers to everything one could come up with. Beer, sodas and rum are offered constantly.A couple of nights various sellers come to the hotel and set up stalls there prices are sky high, yet mainly the German and French tourists will spend crazy money on stuff it seems.To summize: the hotel is good, the food is fair, the staff are friendly, the grounds are meticulously kept, the beach and weather are great, the agrovation of trying to buy something was not worth the effort though - the attitude of the sellers is disgracefull only topped by the attitude of the GERMANS (tons of them) and FRENCH - they push in front of you in a line.A very relaxing 7 days but will try somewhere else next year though.email me with questions papabear02649@yahoo.com

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wished we'd stayed longer We spent a week there, from 3-10 March, and would have stayed longer if we could! It has to go down as one of the most relaxing, hassle-free holidays ever. The check-in around 6.30 pm after a 10 hour flight from UK was very smooth, complete with welcome cocktail, and we were unpacking in the room within 10 minutes. The standard rooms are fairly basic, but functional. I believe the superior ones are a bit better. We were at the end of the 2nd block, on the ground floor, so the outlook wasn't fabulous (onto gardens) but it was conveniently situated for everything, and quiet. Blocks 4 and 5 have a better outlook but apparently a bit noisier. The food was more than adequate, although the buffet gets a bit repetitive. If you're smart, you never have to have the same thing twice, because there is a huge variety of dishes. Breakfasts are about the best spread I've ever seen. We ate in the a la carte restaurant just once, and were a bit disappointed with the service, although the food was good. The trattoria was good for lunchtime pizza, and the 24hr grill was great for burgers/chips at almost anytime. Drinks were quite adequate. The 24 hour all inclusive is a really good package, and the water/soft drinks in the rooms are restocked regularly. Pool and beach are wonderful - except for all the shade chairs being reserved from early in the morning. The entertainment team is enthusiastic, but not very talented. We didn't bother to stay awake very long at night. It would have been nice to have had more live music, with more of a Caribbean sound, to dance to - but this didn't spoil our holiday. I had a massage one afternoon, 30 minutes for $25, which I thought was very good. The facilities are generally well kept and clean. Check-out was also particularly trouble-free, taking about 5 minutes!The only jarring note of the holiday was the $80 each we paid to take a trip to Saona Island. We didn't think it worth the money. The catamaran cruise back was basically no more than a very loud, frenetic booze-cruise. Do go along if you're under 30 and you want to knock back as much rum as possible in 90 minutes. The time on Saona Island was fairly pleasant, but no more so than the beach at LTI.Can thoroughly recommend this resort for good value, comfort, and an all round pleasurable experience.

<Content>Very small and relaxing resort We just returned on Feb.26. 3 of them are there for the second week and will enjoy the sun a little while longer. No problem with check in. We had a room in building One, which I do recommend. Very quite. Not a far walk from the pool, restaurants and beach. Pool was WONDERFUL... Get up early as everyone reserves chairs... So I went with the flow and always got the five chairs under a hut...Food: there is always something for any food preferance to eat. Breakfast was great, omelettes, eggs, bacon, toast. pretty much anything you would want. Lunch: you have your choice of the buffet ( which we never did), the grill; chiken was great, burgers, fries, hot dogs, the pizza was great at lunch at the italian restaurant ( thin crust and many choices). Dinner: we tried it all, Italian restauarnt was good, seafood restaurant was great. We paid for the great seafood and steaks and the buffet was also very good. You always had a wide variety. There was roast beef, wonderful turkey, pasta every night if you want... Great desserts always... Beach is beautiful. I walked a couple of hours everyday... It was always windy, which I did enjoy. We, unfortunately had a couple of days of no sun and rain... Oh well, nothing you can do about that. No real good shopping. VERY pushy vendors and not much choice. My only really bad comment was the housekeeping. They did not reach our room until 5:30pm. At this time we were always napping and our neighbors were getting their kids ready for dinner. was not a convenient time to be cleaning rooms.... Some days they only cleaned half the room( made new beds but did not touch the bathroom). The nightly shows were the same as every other resort. Very amateur... But still a nice time to enjoy an after dinner drink. I saw that the children enjoyed the earlier show that they were all involved in. The disco was quiet, but for a $6 cab ride, you can find a few good party spots. Try the Casino at the Princess Tower as well, only a five minute ride and free shuttle. I enjoyed this resort because it was small and quite.....I read all day, which is exactly what I was looking for. It seemed to be a great place for families as well.. We found the ENTIRE staff very friendly. The language barrier was not a problem. they were always very friendly with us.. They get you up to dance at the outdoor night and the Manager's cocktail party. Would I go back. No.. This is for two reasons: I saw other beautiful resorts there that I would like to try and I also like to go to different islands every year. BUT, if you are going, you should enjoy yourself. the International blend is great. Canadians, Americans, Germans, Italians and South Americans. PS. saw mosquitoes only on th first night and none of us got really sick. Just a few upset stomachs... Take Immodium and that should do the trick...

<Author>tiger99
<Content>Best Beach Area HI, we just got back from a week at the LTI. Overall we were satisfied. The only reall complaint we would have would of been some of the food. It is a german owned resort and lots of germans stay here so they do cater to them a bit more with the food. The buffet - we liked the breakfast you can get omlettes, eggs, pancakes, crepes, bacon, cereal,fruit and tons of other german and dominican things. For lunch and supper the main course changed every day so we liked it some times and not so much other times the pasta was good each time we had it. Now the ala carte restaurants were so so the italain one the menu is just pizza and then you go up and do buffet style for the rest. Us personally did not care for the pizza. It's thin crust pizza there but it's just not like at home. The other ala carte was what they call a seafood restaurant. We ate there twice. One side of the menu is included in your all incl. the other side you pay in us dollars if you want something from that section. There is not a whole lot of seafood on the incl side. There is four main dishes to choose from and then soup  salad as well.We liked the food we had ordered just wish you could of gotten steak without having to pay extra. The snack bar/grill was pretty good for the most part. Hamburgers, hotdogs, chicken, ribs, baked potatoes, fries, etc. it changed a bit each day as well. Always burgers and fries though. One thing this resort is lacking in their snack bar is stuff like popcorn,nacho chips and salsa, appetizer type things. We found latter in the evenings we were craving things like that and could not get them. Only burgers, hotdogs  fries for the most part.The lounges were great with the drinks quite strong so you sometimes had to tell them not so much. The beer we quite liked and the COCO LOCOS.The nightly entertainment we enjoyed it was quite funny at times.One night we had dancers from Santa Domingo come and preform they were great. The rooms are clean nothing super fancy but nice. The beach in front of Lti is super nice we think it was the best part. Now if you want a beach hut you have to get up at the crack of dawn to save one. We never did. But we saw lots of saved ones. Saw one saved in front of us one day and noone came the whole day we were there. We never had trouble finding 2 lounge chairs. All in all we were satisfied with this resort. Would we stay there again probably not just so we could see other properties and have more variety of foods we may like.It is definately not a bad place to stay. We never got sick once. Didn't have any stomach trouble till a bit when we got home. Did get lots of bug bites though. I have over 30 bites on my legs. Husband has some as well. Don't really know when we were getting bit. Saw some bugs but not tons. Well if your going there have a great time we sure did. Ps. they don't have washcloths in the rooms, and you need lots of sunscreen!

<Author>Dennis07
<Content>Had a great vacation My wife and I just returned on Feb. 11 after a 2 week stay. We have stayed at various resorts over the years ( Bali, Cook Islands, Fiji, Mexico (X3), Hawaii (X2)Cuba (X3),Barados, St.Lucia, Canary Islands,etc.)This was our first time to Punta Cana. The beach is a long stretch of white sand and you can walk forever.There is a coral reef approx. 800 meters off shore so there is little undercurrent but the water is choppy and full of sand so no snokelling. The pools are great. The accomodation varies and ours in building #5 was wonderful. It was clean and had a fridge with drinking water provided. We took our own water bottles to fill for travel as water is provided in large 4 liter jugs. There are plentiful loungers but need to be early for the good spots. Most of the guests were from Germany , and Canada with a few from France and USA. The staff always tried to understand our English and were very helpful and we got to practice a bit of Spanish, French and German. The food was very good as they feed approx. 900 people 4X per day.Lots of variety and the service was excellent. There is a grill going 24 hours per day.The beer is good but the wine is not so good. Two annoyances-the entertainment was often crude as they tried to embarass guests and guest smoking up wind with no consideration of others. Overall it was relaxing, the service was great, the food was plentiful and a wide variety of choices, but the entertainment was often too crude for most people.

They all have a special price just for you but you do not need to pay anymore than 1/2 of what they initially ask for.Over all, we had a super time. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Rooms available here for those begging to get sick... I wish I had read more accurate reviews prior to leaving for the LTI Beach Resort in Punta Cana. Now that I've been back for a week (returned on Jan 3/05), feeling completely ripped off and cheated from what was supposed to be an escape from home....I find myself reading reviews on this site that reflect a mirror image of my VACATION!If you are lucky enough to check these reviews (including mine) before you go, please keep these points in mind:-There is still construction going on- the workers start at 7:30am and finish around 8:00 pm. They had bulldozers outside of our room most of the time making alot of noise and stirring up alot of dust, we could not use the balcony most of the time.HOW DO I KNOW THIS...-I fell victim to whatever is going around this resort/ area. After my second day at the resort (after a steak dinner at the Estrella de Mar restaurant), I experienced severe stomach cramps, diarrhea, fever, and nausea/vomiting. We contacted the hotel doctor immediately (4 hours later he arrived with a bag full of Immodium equivalents). I was isolated to the hotel room for 3.5 days with little relief....except for the construction outside...-The doctor is expensive (I was charged $370 US for plug up pills). Be smarter than me, do not accept the individual tablets (loperimida) to relieve symptoms, he charges you for them and he'll wait a few days (at your expense) before he prescribes more effective medication. He will tell you it's not a bug/parasite, it's from the combination of foods you've been eating...I'm waiting for my test results two weeks later and still feeling some of the symptoms listed above. Find outside medical expertise if you can.-The beach and casino are the reasons to come here. If that's what you're looking for, it's here. I've seen several nicer beaches in the Carribbean, but this beach is in the top five.-This resort caters to families, there is little evening entertainment for younger couples. There are lots of activities and babysitting for kids (from what I observed). We found this resort gets really quiet after 10 pm. The only evening activity worth doing was the casino.-The food....I guess I'm biased. The buffet style mixed with the outdoor element of these restaurants leads me to believe a bug/parasite could thrive in this environment and thus explain why so many people are getting sick at this resort. My suggestion is to go the restaurants when mealtimes begin, the food will not be out for very long. At the end of our trip when I could safely eat again, I isolated all of my meals at the Bucannero Grill and did not have any condiments...but these are choices you will need to make for yourself.I will not go back to this resort. I will probably not go back to the Dominican Republic because of my terrible experience, and that's a shame because it seems to be a very beautiful place with lots of things to do.If I do go back, I'm going to do my research more thoroughly and stick with a five star (I hear Secrets Excellence is good..).

<Rating>2	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overall a good holiday We spent two weeks at LTI from Dec 24 to Jan7. Also some family (8 people) from the USA joined us for the first week. This is a long review -so go get a cup of coffee!GENERAL AND ROOMSIf you have already booked with LTI and are now researching don't worry - you should have a great time. The resort is nicely landscaped (and compared to others on the strip that we visited on walks along the beach). The beach is very nice and close to the rooms so you dont have a massive walk back and forth. We (and 2 others from our party) had upgraded rooms in block 5 - great ocean views. Also our TV's worked - no one elses did -and they were not fixed. The air con in our room was marginal - but good enough for December. Generally the room was OK - the maid service is quite cursory really - certainly not as rigorous as a true 4 star resort. The maids do tend to leave the doors open so flies can get in- take a swatter with you -or spend 5 mins when you get in squashing them (no biggie really). RESORTThe resort is quite small but very pretty. The pool is large but a lot of people thought it was too cool. It was certainly refreshing. The tub/whirlpool was not working. There are plenty of seats around the pool and several stands to get braids etc. The braid service along the beach (walk to the beach turn left and walk about 5 mins - lots of vendors there) is better and cheaper. Look out for the guy by the pool who does hand-painted tee shirts -he is amazingly good.FOODThere are only two places to eat around the pool area during the day - both are good. The pool side-grill does fries (get them hot and fresh -they are regularly replenished) burgers and various dogs/sausages. The other place does pizza at lunch-times. Also good. There are two bookable restaurants - you do this at the entrance to the buffet in the morning. Both are good (I thought). The Italian does pizza lasagne etc and the seafood place a variety of stuff (not all seafood). Other than that you have to eat at the buffet. Our group was mixed on this. Some people liked it (I did not). You can find something to eat sure - but I personally dont want rice and beans every day. Others in our group liked the grill at the buffet and the eggs and omlettes in the morning. Personally I found them undercooked. It is no big deal really the pool-side grill is open all the time. It is a bit too much bbq all the time - but some of the salty sausages were great,ILLNESSWell this seems to be the big talking point. None of us got really sick. But we all had some complaints. Second day two people had cramps and one was taking an immodium a day -just to keep going. I felt nauseated on the third day but an immodium put that to rest. I got diahrrea toward the end too - pepto bismol is a must. My take on this -- there is problem at this resort with hygeine. I have never been sick (in any way) at the many many places I have been to (Jamaica, Mexico, Columbia, St Thomas, Antilles, Bahammas... and DR twice before). You can limit your chances of getting ill by not eating salads and cold cuts - watch the glasses (take your own mugs or use the plastic ones) - never use the tap water for anything (except showers obviously). Ease into the diet - be conservative -if others in your group get sick - stay conservative.BARSThere are several bars. The pool-side bar is the most convenient to get to but is poor for cocktails. Beware of the woman's bloody marys - the worst I have ever had. Some were undrinkable. The calypso bar and the lobby bar are much better for mixes. Beer is fine - but tends to be better at the calypso.ENTERTAINMENTI only was one show - and it was great. Very professional. I missed the performance of CATS but it was also supposed to be very good. The kids show runs too late really - also if you have small kids then u may want to go elsewhere - because there are so many German-speakers on the resort the kids dont like to go to the kids club becuase there are no other kids who speak English.WATER SPORTSKatermeran rides up and down the coast are free and good too. Also para sailing and power boat rides - but they cost.BUGSThe resort has a lot of flies. You get used to them (at least I did) but it is annoying. I do not recall any bugs at all on the other resort we stayed at in Punta Cana (Flamenco Bavaro) - we visited that place one affternoon -and indeed I saw no bugs at all.STAFFIn comparison the other resorts the staff seem a bit bit distant and not too interested. SO big deal -I did not go on holiday for their company. The staff could be better -very slow to respond in general -but it did not make or break the holiday.OVERALLNot a bad place really. We did not want to spend a lot of money over Christmas (expensive enough anyway) so we went a bit cheaper. The resort is overall a bit better than 3 stars but not a 4. I doubt I would recommend it to a friend - but there really is nothing too wrong . It does feel a bit too much like you went to Germany after a week or so - dont get me wrong I didn't go to meet Candians and Americans - but the population is a bit too skewed.All of our party had a good time. None of our group had much to complain about - and we didn't hear too much about sickness. But don't leave without that immodium and pepto bismol!

<Content>Win some, lose some Returned form the LTI on Dec 31...after staying for 1 week with my family(son, daughter  son-in-law) from Dec. 24. First a big THUMBS DOWN to Air Transat who since last summer advertised and promoted a direct flight from Thunder Bay to Punta Cana (and kept $4000 on my money for 3 months) on Saturdays, then 3 weeks before we were to leave, cancelled the ENTIRE SEASON LEAVING HUNDREDS OF THUNDER BAY PASSENGERS SCRAMBLING!So our option was to go a day earlier and make (terrible) connections through Toronto...but on to the resort. I was hesitant about going because of all the reviews about sickness. But we prepared ourselves medically (shots. Immodium, malaria pills etc. ) and WE STILL GOT SICK AT THIS RESORT. The food is not that great but what I think the problem with this resort is that 90% of it's food preparations and presentation is buffet style which is very condusive to bacteria with many people handling it and picking through it. The seafood restaurant is very tiny and very difficult to get into..it's the only one that serves dinner individually. Even the Italian restaurant is primarily buffet style with only the pizzas being prepared and served individually.Good Stuff: -beautiful grounds, nice size, fabulous pool and beachRooms are OK but the maid service was very SLOW to respond to requests (eg. one of the bedspreads and pillow were very smelly and musty...3 days later and 4 calls..I finally got clean ones back.)The chambermaids on our floor were VERY LOUD every morning starting about 7:30 am and starting yelling in Spanish and throwing things around almost as if their mandate was to wake everyone up, get them out of their rooms so they could clean up and leave for the day! So, I guess the bottom line is that this hotel is OK for the price but if you are susceptible to food illnesses - do not go to this resort.P.S. North Americans were the minority here-mainly Europeans -the food choice reflected this and so did the number of ladies topless on the beach. Also, some of the staff were very nice - the other half were very discourteous for being in the hospitality industry...but one can get that at any resort. Lots of chairs at the pool and beach for everyone and the beach had a large number of thatched umbrellas for shade. Finally, I was pleasantly surprised by the entertainment offered in the evening ... it was far better than I have seen at much larger resorts!Book all your activities through the staff at the sportsactivity desk..they give you better rates than the company Turissimo - that Air Transat deals with.

<Content>Dancing with the Grim Reaper in the Dominican Republic The LTI resort at Punta Cana, Dominican Republic was the worst vacation experience of my life. My Caribbean traveling experience: I鈥檝e been to the Caribbean over 10 times; (Cuba 2x, Grand Cayman 1x, Jamaica 6x, Dominican Republic 1x).The first thing they tell you after you arrive in Punta Cana is to not drink the water. This was a real confidence booster and made me wonder, what the food is prepared/cleaned with and other possible indirect ways of coming into contact with contaminated water or something else dangerous to ones health?I am a 40 year old from Toronto, Canada. I became very sick at the LTI resort only 2 days after my arrival after eating a fish entree at one of their al la carte restaurants. For the following 5 straight days I practically chained myself to my hotel room bathroom, which I quickly declared a bio-hazard. I've have never been that sick before in my life, and one night I was very close to surrendering to a doctor because I just didn't think I could make it through the night. If it wasn't for a few travel industry friends that I met on the bus from Canada who supplied me with anti diarrhea drugs (Imodium), I don't think I could have survived it without a doctor. I kept tossing and turning in bed with stomach pains, dreaming of dancing with the Grim Reaper. I was most likely poisoned by the food; my guess is probably something in the Salads, Dressings, or the Fish. I think this is a classic case of Traveller鈥檚 Diarrhea I recommend that travelers do a google search on the keywords: 鈥淭raveller鈥檚 Diarrhea鈥? It also didn鈥檛 help my recovery that while bed ridden in my hotel room I had to listen to industrial construction machinery working up until 11pm every evening building a new resort next to the LTI resort.Almost every Canadian I met at the LTI resort in Punta Cana got sick like I did from something or other and strangely enough, quite a few got hit in the same time frame as me, specifically, 2 or 3 days after their arrival. It was almost becoming a bad joke, wondering who was going to fall ill next. I blame LTI for serving me poison at one of their resort hotels and ruining my $1,600 holiday. But I鈥檝e learned from it. I will stick to smaller resorts, not huge tourist resort 鈥淔eeding factories鈥?like LTI. I expected a lot more from a German owned resort. I think LTI has failed miserably in operating a safe and healthy resort.If food poisoning wasn鈥檛 enough to worry about, on Nov 30th up pops a serious travel health advisory on the Public Health Agency of Canada website. I read this Canadian Government advisory online in the LTI Internet room where they offer free internet access. Basically, there are now reports of Canadians, Americans and Europeans returning home from Punta Cana with Malaria. This is the now the limit. After receiving this new news I immediately told the people that I met there to be careful and on my last day I even gave away my insect repellent to a young British couple. I am thankfully back at home now and have been following current developments in the newspapers, specifically, coverage of the Malaria outbreak in the Dominican Republic. Do a search on the Toronto Star website on the keyword: 鈥淢alaria鈥? Media sources say people returning from Punta Cana must monitor themselves for fever for the next 3 months or so and are prohibited from donating blood. I鈥檒l keep my fingers crossed. I am seeing my doctor this week just to give him a heads up. So far I鈥檝e been ok, and haven鈥檛 experienced fever since my return. My fingers are crossed.Other personal observations: The LTI resort landscaping is beautiful and the beach is nice.The Internet room is a welcome free service, but users become quickly frustrated when their online login sessions with the ISP time out so quickly and often. Some even lose all the data in their E-mail compositions. Remember to copy and paste a backup!An large, diverse, and interesting mixture of Europeans and North American tourists at the resort. I sometimes felt like I was at the United Nations.The prices at the LTI gift shop were a complete joke. I didn鈥檛 buy a single thing. For example, a name brand bottle of suntan lotion would be priced at $40U.S. or a simple Chocolate bar would be $5 U.S. This in my opinion is price gouging.The Coffee throughout the resort comes out of commercial name brand machines. I expected real coffee at a Caribbean resort.I was not impressed by the buffet the few times I ate there. (For 5 days I was unable to eat anything). As thirsty as one gets in the Caribbean I was always afraid of drinking the water even if it came from the Buffet or bar water dispensaries. I stuck to the bottled water in my hotel fridge and bottled pop.Finally by the Sunday, the last day of my visit to the Dominican I began to feel a little better and was able to eat some (safe) food (French Fries) at dinner time. I began making progress towards stability. In my opinion, if you travel to Punta Cana, Dominican Republic, you're playing Russian roulette with your health and safety. I love the Caribbean, it鈥檚 just so beautiful, but next time I am going to an island which I feel is safer and where I can avoid the nightmare that I have so far survived in the Dominican Republic. I was never so happy to return home in my life.

<Author>jude
<Content>LTI OK but not for me We stayed at the LTI from Nov 11th- 18th 2004. Let me start by saying the weather was not very nice, rain 4 out of 7 days so that did not help. I have travelled quite a bit over the last 6 years and I am very easy to please, I am not a complainer.Reception - we were greeted at reception with a nice cold drink after a 3 hour bus ride because of road construction. Front desk staff was not very friendly, check in was quick and when we tried to ask about safes etc we were told come back tomorrow. Room - We were put in a room with 2 single beds pushed together (we are 2 married women travelling) so we went to the front desk and asked to be moved to a room with 2 Doubles or Queens, this seemed to be a huge request and we were told the hotel was full period end of story. At which point I went to our Air Transat rep (a plug for them everytime I have had a problem, and I have travelled with them lots, they clear it up immediately) she had us moved by 2 pm that afternoon into a nice room in building 4. The rooms are average size, nothing fancy and what people have written on this site about the location of the toilets is true, I'm 5'3 and it was tight! Service - the maid service was ok again nothing special our room was never cleaned before 4 pm and we were out of it by 8:30 - 9:00 at the latest.The wait staff at the hotel at first seemed very eager and as the week progressed got grumpier and grumpier, maybe the weather was getting to them to. We did tip well and consistently but for us it did not seem to make a differance in service.Food: The food at this resort is ok, I wouldn't describe it as bad but I wasn't going back for 2nds and I didn't gain any weight on this trip which is unusual for me. The seafood restaurant was good but I was dissappointed that most of the seafood was on the menu that had a charge for it, I had grilled Prawns for $13 US and they were delicious. We went to the Italian restaurant one night and all that was on the menu was pizza, it was good but even some of them had charges so we were dissappointed in that.Overall:This resort is German owned so naturally caters to mostly German clientelle. Majority German, then Italian, French and a few English people. We did not find the Europeans to be rude. However we did feel somewhat invisible as 2 english speaking Canadians.Go and see the staff at the dive shop, we met Doreen there and she was great, we went on a Excursion to Catalina Island (Caribbean side) with them with a bus and boat full of Germans and Russians it was a fabulous day and the highlight of our vacation.The Ocean: Be aware that you are in the Atlantic Ocean and the pictures you see in brochures etc are probably taken in June, July. The Ocean is rough and it is very windy, red flag at the dive shop the whole time we were there so no watersports. We had envisoned snorkelling, sailing, or some sort of watersport everyday off the beach, not! The people we talked to there said that it is usually windy and waves for most of the winter however in January February they don't get as much rain.We went on this trip just to relax so we didn't venture outside the resort other than the one tour. The hotel did have 3 English movie channels so we caught up on our TV and our sleep. Feel free to e-mail any other questions.

I along with my wife and 21 month old son stayed at the resort from 7 - 21 October 2004.Having read some of the reviews, a lot of which were poor ones, we were slightly worried about this hotel before we got there. I have to say that our concerns were groundless and I'm sure the poor reviews posted earlier must be about a different hotel because this one is fantastic!Accommodation - we were situated in block 2 of 5. Whilst there was a hotel being constructed next door, this did not distract at all. Obviously a view of the pool or the beach would have been better but this didn't distract from our holiday as we didn't spend much time in our room anyway. The rooms were spotless although a little dated perhaps. The cleaning staff were excellent and there were clean towells and sheets every day.Food - the food was excellent in all the restaurants we tried. The choice and quality were amazing. The waiting staff were very attentive, always topping up drinks before you had a chance to ask.The Staff - the staff were so friendly and professional it was untrue. The animation team were great but the guys that make the whole place tick are the 4 Italian reps from Eurotravel (Pier, Valario, Andrea and Alice). Whilst not employed by LTI they were mainly responsible for the beach and pool games and the shows in the evenings. They really did make our holiday. My advice would be to get involved with the activities as it really is great fun.The Beach - the beach is simply stunningThe Pool - again stunning and very clean and safe for kids.We took our 21 month old son with us and he was treated like royalty by the staff!! He had an absolutely fantastic time. Whilst there wasn't a great deal on offer for him, the pool and beach were enough. The only slight critism it that the only play area is set up for older children and they could do with catering for the younger kids too. There is a kids club available for 4 years+ but dont know how good this was.The fellow guests were very friendly. I have read poor reports about German guests but from my experience this could not be further from the truth. The Germans I met were very very friendly. There were not many English speaking guests, mainly Germans and Italians but to be honest I dont go to foreign countries to see other British people!!! It was much more fun communicting by some sort of sign language or broken French or whatever!!Overall we had the best holiday ever and we were very sad to leave after 2 weeks which simply flew by.Would I go back to the Dom Rep? Without doubt!Would I stay at this hotel again? Absolutely

<Content>LTI - Great Family Vacation My wife and I and our two daughters, aged 7 and 3, traveled to LTI Beach Resort in Punta Cana for two weeks in March 2004. It was our first trip to DR after several trips to Cuba and Florida. We chose LTI because it featured kid鈥檚 activities and the property looked great in the web photos. When we walked through the lobby onto the grounds, we were amazed at the beauty. The landscaping and level of maintenance was excellent 鈥?very lush and tropical. We had a premium room on the 3rd floor in building 5, right on the beach next to the dive centre. The room was a good size, clean with a great view of the ocean. We liked the stocked fridge 鈥?water and pop daily! We only saw 2 lizard-critters in the room and had some ant colonies set up shop after the kids left some cookies out in the open. Watch the tile floors with wet feet 鈥?very slippery! The resort had a good 鈥渧ibe鈥?and the pool area was the place to be as it was central to most of the facilities. Some resorts in Punta Cana are so huge and sprawled out that there is no sense of community. We met a lot of people there and it was interesting to talk with people from Canada, USA and Germany. The beach was the best part of our stay, and since we walked the beach a couple of kilometers daily in either direction, we were convinced our stretch of beach was the best. It had a shallow, gradual slope and small waves due the reef just off shore. Other parts of the beach south of LTI had huge waves, strong undertow and steep slopes into the water 鈥?not kid-friendly. Our stay included water sports and we took out the catamaran, body boards and my wife learned to scuba dive and took her first open-water dive on the only stormy day we had in two weeks 鈥?I guess when you鈥檙e underwater it doesn鈥檛 matter if it鈥檚 raining! The kids had a great time in the kids club with Bea from Germany. She was very patient with the kids and had a variety of activities to keep them busy. They still talk about her. The evening entertainment was a kiddy-show and games before the stage show began at about 9PM. The stage show was predictable and hokey most times, although when they brought in a DR folk music band and dancers the professionalism and enjoyment went way up. They did play some interactive games with the audience which I made a fool of myself in a couple of times! Good thing we were too tired at night to expect too much! We didn鈥檛 go to the bar/disco but we saw it in the day and it was about the size of my living room. I think the real parties happen elsewhere. The internet caf茅 was a great way to keep an eye on the bank account and email and the cost was reasonable. North along the beach from LTI is strip of shopping huts along the beach, you can get everything there, but don鈥檛 buy anything on your first few days 鈥?the vendors can sense your vulnerability. Check out all the shops and don鈥檛 feel intimidated by their 鈥渋n your face鈥?sales pitch. My wife bargained these guys so hard they gave her things to get rid of her. The big gimmick down there is that Mamajuana / DR Viagra 鈥?it tastes like crap and Canada Customs won鈥檛 let it into Canada. The best deals are on the beach. When you go on tours and stop into tourist trap gift shops, save your money and buy your souvenirs on the beach. We went on the Bavarro Runner full day excursion and it was a full day: sugar cane plantation, homesteads, horseback riding, cigar shop, etc. If you have spoiled kids take them and show them how kids on the plantation live, they might learn to appreciate what they have back at home. I bought some nice vanilla flavoured cigars at the cigar tour, very nice and reasonable price. Drinks and a meal are included on the tour; it was pricey but an exciting experience. The food was good and they had a good variety with no theme repeated in the whole 2 weeks that we were there. The Italian restaurant was really good and even my Italian wife thought the food was prepared well. We loved the Neptune pizza. The grill by the pool was never crowded and when you鈥檙e in mood for meat and potatoes, the grill is the place to be. Breakfasts were the great 鈥?bacon, eggs, fruits and the best, melt-in-your-mouth croissants you鈥檒l ever taste. You can smoke everywhere, so militant non-smokers should save their 鈥済lares of disgust鈥?for back home 鈥?different culture 鈥?different rules! Finally, we flew out of Hamilton, Ontario, Canada on West Jet instead of Toronto and what a pleasant experience that was! No traffic, no lines and we were home in 15 minutes. LTI Beach Resort has set the benchmark for quality and value in a holiday! We would go back without any doubt.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Very Good Vacation Experience. Just returned from a week at LTI. Even rode out Hurricane Jeanne! Our travel to Punta Cana was Sept. 11 to 18, 2004. This was our first trip to the Dominican Republic and Punta Cana.This is a beautiful Resort. The grounds are nicely landscaped and well groomed. Lots of green, lots of flowers, and very nicely laid out. The lobby area is open concept, simple yet functional, with a thatched roof and a pleasant lobby bar.There are some small gift shops and bank and a hair salon in the resort. You can use U.S. dollars or convert to Dominican Pesos. We just used dollars even off resort.We found the food in the main buffet restaurant to be of good quality with lots of variety, in a mainly carribbean style with other theme nights adding to variety as well. We always looked forward to meal-times. The a la carte restaurants were pleasant, and food was excellent.Many of the resort staff spoke English, and we used a Spanish / English phrase book to help out when needed. Our efforts to do so were appreciated by the staff who were always friendly and helpful.The resort has a beautiful beach and lots of watersposts activities available. Also Beach volleyball and beach soccer were played.The pool is gorgeous and has a kiddie pool as well. This is a good place for families with small children.Our room was large and kept very clean with the fridge stocked daily with pop and bottled during the regular daily maid service.My son-in-law and myself had some stomach discomfort on our third day, but we took medication and the symptoms were pretty much gone the next day. Never really interfered with our activities or total enjoyment.Hurricane Jeanne arrived on the evening of our 5th day there, and the resort's building and structures weathered the storm very well. We felt completely safe in our rooms where we didn't even feel the wind. The storm did blow a little water seepage into our room at the patio doors making the floor damp in some areas, but the room and our possessions remained dry. From what we could see, all of the guest room buildings were left pretty much untouched by the hurricane winds and heavy rains.There was minor damage to some of the other buildings, like missing shingles and some damage to thatched roofs, but no structural damage to the resort buildings themselves.Lots of trees were blown over or broken, and the grounds had a lot of debris right after the storm, but within 24 hours the staff had most of the clean-up well under way.Other Punta Cana resorts were more heavily damaged and their guests were transported to resorts with less damage. LTI maintained electrical power throughout the storm with its own generators although there were revolving black-outs as repairs were being made. We had short black-outs on running water in our rooms as well. It took a little longer for them to restore hot water for showers etc.The phone service was out for about a day.Some staff members had their own homes demolished by hurricane Jeanne, but remained on site to keep the resort fuctioning as much as possible. Some were even putting in 15 to 20 hour work-days to cover for staff who were unable to make it to work right after the storm.A few of the tourists brought into our resort from other places which had sustained more damage were complaining about some pretty trivial concerns. (None relating to LTI) You can tell what is really important to people when you see how they deal with unexpected adversity. From what we could see LTI did an outstanding job in providing for us throughout the ordeal.Would I go back to LTI Beach Resort. Absolutely!What about the negative reviews of LTI on this site?Everyone has their own opinions, expectations and experiences. Ours was very positive. and this was our 6th Carribbean all inclusive vacation in 7 years and the first at this location.All in all, we had a great vacation experience and would encourage others to consider this resort.

<Content>Great Vacation I vacationed the week of August 13 thru the 20th. My husband and I traveled with our two children and my mother.
