When we got off the plane the driver took us directly to the resort in an air-conditioned mini van. Our rooms were not ready so we went to have lunch and by the time we came back we were ready to go to our rooms. I don鈥檛 understand how people complain about the food. There is so much too choose from. The people that work there were wonderful, very helpful and accommodating. I traveled with my children age 6 and 4 and they loved the young women named Bella that is in charge of the Smiley club. They spent 4 hours of the day with her and they loved dancing and singing in the shows every night. There is some truth to some of the emails. What I found not true is about the Germans being rude. Everyone we encountered was very pleasant. I believe this idea comes because of the language barrier. Of course I could not communicate but everyone smiled and said 鈥渉ola鈥?which is hello in Spanish. I did not find any special treatment for anyone. Of course I did have an advantage knowing the language but you must expect when traveling to any country or island that has a different language or culture that you will find some barriers in communication. The people from the activity committee, the check in counter and even the Kids club all spoke a minimum of 4 languages. I found the show very good they had some professional dancers that did a great job and a magician that was great. The only show that was poor was the Karaoke night and that depends on the audience. If you go expecting a Broadway show or a cruise ship show you will be disappointed. Every night we laughed and enjoyed the games and shows. The group of guys and girls that are in charge of the activities and games do a great job. They do a wonderful job presenting the shows. So suggestions would be to take plenty of singles for tips these people get paid so little the greatly appreciate tips. I got all my jewelry that I don鈥檛 ware and picked up a couple of items from the dollar store and I would leave a couple of items with two dollar for the cleaning lady, she made sure our refrigerator was stocked up. I did not like that the merchants are very persistent for you to purchase from them. Make sure you bring your toiletries, sun block, sun lotions, and basic stomach medications. They sell them in their stores but for outrageous prices. For example sun tan lotion was $20.00 us dollars. Drop by and look at Leonard鈥檚 Hanna tattoos we all got tattoos and had a wonderful conversation with him. Tattoos lasted about 2 weeks and very reasonable price; I wish we had them here in the states. My husband paid for a message but was a bit disappointed because it was supposed to be for 30 min. and the girl left the room lots of times so it ended up more like 15 to 20 min.Pay after you have gotten your services done. I was tempted to get the braids on my hair so I would not have to care for it but I have very long hair and new it would take hours so I opted not to but they look beautiful on all the girls. Over all we had a wonderful vacation and are planning to go again next year just not in August it was awfully hot.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>FABULOUS trip for the money! We got a last minute deal through Vacations Express (I think we paid $299 all-inclusive per person for three nights?) It was more than we could have asked for!The resort itself is very tropical and fun. It's not your classic frou-frou resort, it's more of a beachy, island-y kind of place. The room was gorgeaus and had a view of the ocean. It had a fridge, a king bed (decorated in a really cool tropical motif), and gorgeaus tile and marble floors and walls. Even the bathroom was impressive! The resort itself was great... beautiful beaches, incredible food, LOTS of yummy beer and drinks... just paradise for the money. Here are some of my suggestions:-If you're the type who goes on vacations to drink, lay in the sun, enjoy the beach and the ocean, and eat enough for a small army, this is the place for you! -If you're squeamish about native dishes, don't come here... even their American foods, like hamburgers and hotdogs, have a native taste to them. Everything is either spicy, rich, cheesy or tomatoey... I loved it! -The desserts aren't the best though... bring some cookies or candy if you're a sweet freak.-Bring your own EVERYTHING because everything on the resort is, of course, really expensive, and our tour facilitator suggested that we not go onto the island to go shopping because of recent violence... however, you are very safe in the resort.-Walk down the beach to the beach shops if you want to buy some native arts and touristy goodies... and NEVER pay what these folks tell you it costs! You can generally reduce what they tell you by at least half (i.e. if they tell you the windchime is $40, offer $15 or $20 and then pretend to leave... trust me, they'll take your offer!)Have fun!!!

You have to get up pretty early if you want a seat under a cabana- (which we needed after a day in the sun!). And the pool chairs are first come first serve as well. This means you need to reserve early with your towels or try and find something later in the day. That was sometimes frustrating. (Ironically we always had somewhere to sit!)We had massages by the ladies on the property and they were great. Especially listening to the waves from the beach right next to you.It only rained one day which we didnt mind. We felt pretty lucky that it hadn't rained more. We still swam in the pool and enjoyed the day.I have to say the staff really helps make the resort. They are always willing to help and fill your drinks or whatever. And they are just so happy! They made us laugh a lot. And if anyone is interested there is a Catholic Mass two resorts away at the Bravaro Princess at around 6pm on Sunday night. Overall we truly had a wonderful honeymoon and Dominican experience at LTI. We would go back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Another Great Vacation!!!  Our family just spent the week of June 12th 2004 at the LTI. My husband and I spent a week there in 2002 and were so happy with our vacation we returned again this year with our kids (19 and 22).The beach is beautiful, the pool is sparkling and in April 2002 and June 2004 we never had a problem getting chairs or cabanas, no matter what time of day it was. The rooms are clean and free of insect life. We stayed in building 5 in 2002 which is closest to the beach and farther away from everything else. This year we were in building 4 which I found to be perfect...still close to the beach and a bit closer to the pool and restaurants. I brought a bag of stuff from the dollar store for the maid and each day I left out a few items along with $2. She was thrilled.They appreciate cosmetics, perfume and chocolate. I also brought hair items, lotions, lollypops and chewing gum. The food is excellent with enough variety that even the more fussy eater can find plenty to choose from. The pizza in the Trattoria restaurant is awesome and the atmosphere in the Estrella Del Mar is a nice change from the buffet style restaurants. It is a small enclosed, air conditioned restaurant with some choices that are included in your all-inclusive plan, and other choices that require payment.(both those restaurants are by reservation only for dinner - you make your reservation w/ the hostess at the Mirador buffet in the mornings between 7a.m. and 10a.m.) There is also the Buccanero which is all grilled entrees... burgers, dogs, etc.  Three of us made it through the week with no stomach ailments at all... one of us experienced a day or two of discomfort...but I personally think it was more alcohol related than food related. Do not overdo it on the delicious fruit drinks. Coconut and pineapple both have laxative effects! Same goes for the fresh fruit... eat it in moderation if you are not used to eating alot of fruit in your regular diet. As for the resort being German owned and the complaints of other travelers about the German's rudeness and catering only to the Germans.... we found none of this. The majority of guests are Germans and Europeans but everyone was pleasant and I felt we all got equal treatment from the staff. There were also a number of Canadians and of course others USA travellers.  We did alot of snorkeling, rode 4 wheelers on the beach, horsback riding and para-sailed. The weather was gorgeous all week with rain only at night and little or no wind, just beautiful breezes. My son and I got Henna-Tattoos (they last about 3 weeks) and the guy doing the tattoos is from Czechoslavakia, speaks English and was a pleasure to talk with. Very very nice individual. The tattoos range from $7-$20 and the chameleon I got crawling up my arm was a fun addition to our adventure. The evening entertainment is a bit amateurish but it was still entertaining. The nights where there is audience participation are the best. So funny. In 2002 my husband and I were part of one show and we won 1st place and a lobster dinner. This year my kids each participated in a show and it was great fun. The best piece of advice I can give is go with an open mind and no preconcieved worries from people's poor reviews. Some people are just never happy and like to complain. Remember, you are in another country...their standards are not the same as ours ...a 5 star hotel there is not going to be the equivalent of a 5 star here in the states. And most importantly...have a great vacation...we did! If anyone would like more specific information about anything feel free to send me an e-mail. Please put LTI or Punta Cana in the subject line.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A nice vacation My best friend and I stayed at the LTI beach resort for the week of May 30- June 6 2004. This was our first trip to the Dominican Republic. Overall we had a very good time. The resort staff is all very friendly and accommodating. We stayed in building four in the resort. We were told by our travel agent that there is no construction taking place on the resort. That is not entirely true. Directly behind our room was another resort being built. The construction took place 24 hours a day. Albeit it is not on the LTI property but it is in plain view and can be heard. My friend and I were not all that bothered by the construction as we could rarely hear it in our room however the couple next door to us found it unbearable and requested a room change- which was honoured. The resort itself is much smaller than many of its neighbouring resorts which has its pros and cons. We never had any problems finding a favourable place on the beach or pool side nor did we have difficulty making reservations for the 2 a la cartes. If you are looking for a vacation full of rest and relaxation you will find it here. The nightly entertainment was satisfactory at best. If this is something you look for in a vacation go else where as it needs some work. They do have a disco that no one goes to despite the staff's desperate attempts to have you go. If you want a resort with a good disco go to the Grand Flamenco as the disco there is raved about. We did a number of activities well we were there such as parasailing, snorkelling, and an ATV 4x4 excursion. Be sure to book your activities through the activity centre as oppose to your travel rep on the resort as you will save a bit of money and the excursions are bit better quality in my opinion. If you are at all interested in leaving the resort to explore the neighbouring towns then I would recommend you take the ATV excursion it was with out a doubt worth every dollar. My friend and I were the only ones who signed up for the trip so we ended up getting a private tour. Our tour guide took us to a beautiful beach, a cave (that you could swim in) , a banana plantation, farms, and a near by village were we got to meet his family and friends! If you do go on this trip be sure to bring some things to give to the many children you will see along the way (such as candy/toys).Like many of the other reviews have highlighted the resort is German owned and there are VERY few English speaking people on the resort. Mostly German, Spanish, French, and Dutch. There is a very large language barrier so if you are someone who is looking to meet others while on your vacation it is helpful to be fluent in one of the above mentioned languages. The staff speaks broken English so you shouldn鈥檛 have to many problems communicating with them- we didn鈥檛. Well that is the Coles notes version of our trip. I hope that this was helpful. The resort doesn't have a gym but there are aerobics at 10 am and noon every day and it's fun because they guys not only make you work out but also teach you some choreographies. It's also true that there are a lot of smokers but that is something that you have to accept outside of the US. We hate smoke and the stench of cigarretes but we'd solve this situation by sitting someplace where the breeze would keep the smoke away from us. In sum, don't feel discouraged by some comments here, go see by yourself and allow the Dominican hospitality to make you have an unforgettable vacation. Have fun and feel free to write me if you have any questions about this resort. We are glad we went although at the beginning I felt aprehensive after reading all the negative feedback here.We'll be back next year!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Cayena Review - New addition to the LTI resort Trip Dates: May 1- May 8: My husband and I visited the Cayena Beach Club Resort, which is a new addition to the LTI Resort in Punta Cana. We exchanged our time share to visit the property, and I was having a hard time finding info on the Cayena, and didn't realize it was a resort within a resort. Here's the scoop: LTI built a new building intended to be marketed as a time-share property. The rooms are nicer (suites, marble bathrooms, oceanfront), plus there are other fringe benefits. They release rooms within the new building to SOME, but it is not predictable. You can request a room there (building 6), but it is not guaranteed. I recommend you email the resort directly to request a room in that building.Please note: The entire property is all inclusive. It was a surprise to us that we were required to pay the all-inclusive fee upon arrival, but it was affordable. It was WELL worth it.If you stay at the Cayena, you have access to the entire LTI property, plus private grounds only Cayena folks can use. The LTI grounds are very nice, the pool is great, the food selection is plentiful. The best think about the Cayena is you have a private restaurant by the beach that you can go to for breakfast and lunch. The food is special, as you can have t-bone, tenderloin, and other such food for lunch! More wine is poored before you can empty your glass. In addition, there is a beach-side pool, bar and hot-tub that is for Cayena folks as well. Unlike other reviews I read, I found the staff to be very nice and accomodating. The only challenge is that English is not spoken well (if at all), and you have to adjust. Most visitors are European, thus you can make great friends with the staff by bringing money to tip. It is difficult to get dollar bills, so bring plenty for leaving a buck or two for meals and drinks. The people are kind and hard working and deserve the tips. I read another review recommending you bring large glasses to drink at the pool. Good suggestion!Do not be afraid, Americans! It's a great resort.

<Content>We had a great time This was my first time in the caribbean. My wife and I arrived on Wednesday the 14th of April and stayed for a week. I can't say the German are especially cold or rude (except for one idiot...), but it is hard to socialize with them because of the language barrier. We made up for it by taking on the Bavarro Runner excursion with a francophone group. The food was great at the buffet. There is a very large selection. Try not to taste everything on the same night. We had no problems getting reservations at the pizza and seafood places. The entire resort is very clean. No use trying to get american dollars over there so be prepared to negotiate in pesos. We took a taxi and went to the Bavarro Plaza. There are two cigar factories and a nice jewlery boutique. The hotel employees are very nice, especially if you attempt to order in spanish. I didn't feel as though I had to constantly give tips to get good service. Tips are expected for the cleaning lady and the bagage boy. I had a wonderfull time and I would go back to this place.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it Having read many of the bad reviews I was a little hesitant about what I was going to be seeing when I got to the hotel. I loved it. I loved the lay out of the buildings where the rooms were. I was in #4 and had a view of the ocean. The pool area was lovely and kept very clean. The staff were very friendly. Breakfast....eggs, bacon, sausage, fruit, breads, yogurts. Lunch I usually ate at the Italian restaurant because I loved the pizza and salads there. Dinner... a few types of meat, pototoes, rice, vegetables, fruit, bread......even the fussiest eaters can find something to eat. At the 24 hour grill there was also great hotdogs and sausages and fries. I didn't try the burgers but they looked good too. The bars did a cocktail of the day which I enjoyed trying each day. As I am an early riser and enjoyed getting up to see the sun rise, I was often in bed before the shows started. I did manage to stay up to see Cats and one other show. Not really my cup of tea. Didn't bother with the disco, so have no comment. As I was in building #4 I had no bother from outside noises at night, which I have in other hotels. I tried a few of the trips...Saona Island, Bavaro Trackers (jeep safari) and Bavaro Runners (4x4's), catamaran reef trip and the Aquatic tour.....all were very enjoyable and on most you are encouraged to drink....lots of fun. My only complaint would be that the hotel seemed to be the first pick up and the last drop off, for the trips, so I was always on the bus the longest. I guess somebody has to be first!! Would definately recommend this resort. I found Punta Cana to be a bit more expensive than parts of Cuba but worth it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Our Worst Vacation We returned from Punta Cana on March 9/04. We were there for two weeks and stayed at the LTI for the first week. Nothing went right from the onset. LTI is overbooking because they are just finishing a new VIP building and putting people into it. We were upgraded into this new VIP building. The suite had a living room, but no furniture. We wanted a small table and two chairs, but never did get it. We did get two stacking lawn chairs so we were able to sit in our room. There were no curtains on the windows and we were on the ground floor. We had a dresser in the bedroom, but no mirror above it. There was a large pie shaped bath/shower tub with jets, but no shower curtain. When we showered the water went onto the floor. The keys to the room are the new credit card type. We got two keys, but only one worked. We asked and got the bad key reprogrammed, then the first key did not work. Then vise versa. At the end we still had only one key which worked. We arrived at LTI during the supper hour, so all of next day we were trying to straighen this mess with our room. That evening we were playing cards (on the corner of our dresser) when a rat ran from our closet into our bathroom. We both saw it. My wife freaked out. We called guest services. A young man came with a can of spray, sprayed the closet and bathroom and said no problemo and left. We called guest services and asked for another room, but it was too late and they said - tomorrow. The next day we spent talking to our Tour Rep. After a couple of visits and he talking to the resort management we were able to get another room in the old building. The Tour Rep told us that the only reason we are changing rooms is because the manager owed him one. I found that the bathrooms in the first room we were in have a cold air return, at the floor level, and the louvers are spaced very wide apart, so there is plenty of space for a rat to get through. I removed this cold air vent and saw dirt and pipes. This is a highway for the rats to commute to any room they want in the building. The room in the old building appeared tight and rat proof. We spent the rest of the day packing, moving and unpacking. That night my wife got food poisoning at the buffet. She spent the next 24 hours in our room and would not venture out as she had to stay near the toilet. In addition she had extreme sromach cramps, which lasted for another several days. In addition to the buffet, there are two a la carte restaurants. The Italian served pizza which was totally bland, thin and greasy. The International a la carte restaurant- Well I don't know what the food was like in there as we never got in there there . I estimate that restaurant has 40 to 50 chairs and there are over 1000 guests. I had to be in the line up at 6:30 to 7:00 to make reservations for that night. Thats too much for me. There appeared to be enough chairs on the beach, but if I wanted a chair under one of the grass huts (shaded) I had to be on the beach between 5:30 to 6:30 A.M. to place a towel on a chair to call it reserved. There also are not enough shaded areas around the pool. Once again, this is too much for me and I do not call this a vacation. We go back to our Tour Rep, who now knows us well, to request a transfer out of LTI. In addition to all the problems we had the resort does not have sufficient beach, pool and a la carte facilities which is causing the guests to battle one another into getting there first. I do not call this a relaxing situation for a vacation and we want out. It took two days, but we were able to get out and into our next choice. We did not get any follow up or apology from LTI. To break our contract we had to pay $200.00 plus a $50.00 cost to open a new file for the new resort. Our new resort cost us an additional $300.00 for a total of $550.00. Then, of course, 15$US for cab and another day of packing/unpacking. We spent exactly one week at the LTI and had no vacation, however, our new choice - the Grand Paradise was very satisfactory(with none of the above problems) and we had a good week. Thanks to our great Tour Rep. Without him we would not have been able to get any satisfaction from LTI directly.

<Content>LTI Great vacation spot for the money March 2004. Just returned from LTI Beach Resort, Punta Cana. For the dollar value, this is a good resort. Evening entertainment was pretty good. The LTI is a smaller resort so you have the opportunity to meet some great people from around the world. A lot of the guests are French or German, but a good range of English people as well.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>LTI is recommended We were there from 28 Feb to 6 Mar 2004. TNT vacation. Like many other reviewers I read lots of reviews and frankly wondered if I had made a good choice based on some of what I read. I swear that some of the reviewers are born complainers with sight and hearing problems, and would rate heaven with one star!! So here goes. Remember that the Star rating for these resorts is not the same as rating NYC hotels. Our room was always clean and neat. Leave a note and a couple of bucks and you get extra soda in the refrig. Some complained that there was a musty smell in the room. What does one expect 20 degrees above the equator? I have experienced that at Cape Cod!! That minor annoyance is gone quickly with the more than adequate A/C. The food was above good and it was no worse or better than any other all-inclusive I have been to. Good variety and some of the preparations were excellent (salads, spare ribs, desserts, pizza, pasta). The drinks I had were great...all non-alcoholic. If all these complainers had carefully read all their documents they would have been fore-warned that the booze is all local and name stuff could be obtained for a couple of bucks. My wife said the beer and red wine were good, the white wine not too good. One of the reviewers said the bar service was very slow which we did not experience at all. You don't have to walk very far to a bar anyway..so walk there. 98% of the staff were very helpful and friendly. Complainers frequently start with thier own brand of unfriendliness and that triggers the same response. Do unto others......The beach was nice and the reviewer who was there at the same time as us must have been hallucinating about all the boat traffic. I could count on one hand how many came past our area. Also the beach is far from small and one can walk lirterally over a mile in either direction past other resorts. Nightlife was acceptable but then again I didn't go there for that pleasure. The staff did OK and get a A+ for effort. The idea is to read up as much as possible, remember that you are not going to paradise, keep your expectations reasonable, and start out with a positive attitude and it will come back in abundance. We travelled with our special-needs son and all the staff made alot of him. That is because he is unconditional and doesn't sweat the small stuff. The staff went out of their way to include him in the dancing, ( the Meringe ). One of the stores even gave him a present of a shirt and a pair of flip flops. One of the vendors gave him a present of a good luck necklace. It was nice to see that they seem to know just how Special he is. We thought the Express Check-In was worth the extra price. I am 69 years old. We zipped through at Logan and had front seats on the plane. We also went through Punt Cana airport quickly coming back, again with front seats. I would recommend LTI. Just do your homework to avoid being tripped up by things you weren't aware of.

Iwas seated in an aisle seat and the arm rest had sharp metal coming from it and made 5 tears in my jeans at the hip area.the stewardess said oh I think they were like that when you came on the plane and laughed. Took us 1 hr to get to LTI from the airport, because they dropped off at all the hotels first,ours was the furthest away.You could see the lobbies of all the different hotels as the people got dropped off, they all looked beautiful, and talking with people about the hotels that they stayed at,everyone seemed pleased, and that the 4 and 5 star seemed the same.LTI is a good value.The staff at LTI were some of the happiest people I have ever met, singing, dancing, laughing a lot of the time.The hotel was very clean,there were people cleaning and tending to the grounds all the time.We stayed in building4,they said we had an ocean view,but did not,if we had the 2nd or 3rd floor maybe we would have. we asked to be moved,but we needed 2 rooms together,so we never got moved. We did a couple of excursions-the calypso party boat-$55-not worth it- good rum punch,but the snorkeling was too hard-about 100 people on the boat crashing into you and it was for a total of two hours, 20 min of it was snorkeling. Bavarro runnners was excellent-a must do, 20 people board this huge jeep like truck and they drive you all over the country side so you get to see diiferent parts of punta cana-we stopped at a cigar factory,a sugar cane field, this lady's house named Maria who is world famous for her chocolate and coffee,we saw how cocoa and coffee were made and learned a lot, also saw a cock fight, then onto a little ranch for lunch and a1/2 hr horse back ride around the hills, very pretty, then we went to this deserted beach that was beautiful.we also saw a rice field. we got to see how the ricers fruiters and farmers lived.That tour was $75. and was all day,very nice trip. We also took a 2hr horse back ride 5-7pm great horses, very gentle, and went for about 5miles down the beach with them! we could even run with them, something you would see on tv!! a bargain for$35! this was at the ranch that was right down the beach from LTI!! We were going to go to Santa Domongo for shopping but it was a 3+hr bus ride one way and wicked hot,so we just shopped at the fleamarket on the beach near LTI. what hagglers they are!! often obnoxious,they don't let you alone, about 1/2hr is all I could take of that at a time.they would ask 4x the amount of what something is worth,and you would have to haggle them down. Some good bargains,tshirts $4. got a huge wooden parrot,2 monkeys carved from coconuts and 2 coin purses for $40. Some of the stuff they sell is just pure junk.The shows at night were ok, some very dumb, others good with the dancers. The beds in the rooms were like boxsprings, we had 2 beds in each room,so we piled them on top of one another and that was better. to get a beach cabana you had to be at the beach no later than 7:30am to save one or you were out of luck, plenty of chairs not enough cabanas,nice breeze at the beach all the time, the pool had no breeze and was very hot.water was nice and clean and cool. All in all I loved LTI and would go back there in a heartbeat,plan on returning next year.There are some must bring items when you go.bring an old credit card-your room key holder is this shape and size-you place it in a slot upon entering your room and your a/c and fridge only work when this is in place-this way everything stays cool most of the time. a large plastic thermal cup-like from dunkin donuts-so you can have more than 4oz at a time of ice water or cocktails and it will stay cold for you-they serve drinks in plastic juice cups! saves you from having to keep running from the beach to the bar! bring non dairy creamers with you if you like cream in your coffee, the milk they had for it smelled rancid.bring peptobismal and immodium, I only used this one day but was sure glad I had it. bring powerful sunscreen-I used spf15 all the time, and I tan usually pretty easily,but still burnt a bit. bring about$50 in $1 bills, good for tips and shopping, I brought travelers checks and they were a pain. Get a room safe-about $2/day-worth the piece of mind.bring a small cd player for the beach- we did and it worked out great,the resort was very safe and no one touched our stuff at the beach. bring casual clothes-I packed way too much, usually wore shorts and a tank top, at night shorts and a t-shirt,or capris and a tshirt, didn't have to get dressed up because we couldn't get into the restaurant that you needed to be dressed up for. bring a travel alarm clock, no clocks in the room or anywhere in the resort,CNN on the tv in the room had a clock so that was helpful. They go by Dominican time very laid back, we thought we missed our pick up times for the excursions,but they always ran 1/2hr late! bring a beach bag to bring books,lotions,etc.with you to the beach. Have a wonderful time!!we did and can't wait to go back!!

The wind is constant (which is nice) but may be too strong for the sunfish sailboat that is part of the all inclusive package (have to pay more to use catamaran). <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Winter Break LTI Beach Resort deserves merits for making the Super Bowl available to us. When we got off our plane from Boston, several tour members threatened to board the return flight if the Super Bowl would not be viewable on the following day. apparently our TNT tour guide took the effort, and we began to hear that we would be able to see that game someplace at LTI. By Sunday afternoon the aerobics instructor (?) was carrying a poster around the pool with a message something like the following: See Super Bowl, American football, on big screen with open bar at 7:00 p.m.in discotheque.  My wife and I already had reservations for 6:30 at Trattoria, the Italian sit-down restaurant with pizzas as first course. However, we each ate about half of a very large pizza, and the waiters folded boxes slightly clumsily in front of us. We walked into the discocarrying our pizzas about 7:15, and were greeted by envious guests shouting, Where did you get those? We passed those boxes around, and most of the remains were grabbed up.  There were seats for about 50 guests, and there were about 35 Patriots fans, 8 Carolina fans, and a share of LTI staff people, seemingly from the PE staff (i.e. people like the aerobics instructor) as well as the English Entertainment Director (aut sim.) with his child, wanting to see and receive instruction in American Football.) Several of the guests had come from a neighboring resort, where Super Bowl was not available, and paid a fee to view at LTI and be eligible for open bar. There were initially problems with the reception, which was projection on a movie screen. By midway in the first quarter CBS coverage was available (though the viewing was never perfect), and it was possible to hear their description of the game and see the half-time show. (I'm not saying that was essential viewing, but the news coverage of it on CNN and other channels received in Dominican Republic would have been confusing if we had not had any idea what that was about.)  In the 4th quarter, when the score was 29-23, the entertainment director said (facetiously) You know how this game is going. You've seen enough. I'll just turn this off. We shouted him down, and we saw the game till the tie score was broken in the last minute.  Another real entertainment was the chefs at breakfast preparing the fried eggs and ommelettes. Guests were able to select ingredients for omelettes from bowls on the line and hand them to chefs. The chefs spilled olive oil on the gridle, broke eggs, holding one in each hand, mix them up, drop eggs on the gridle, and add the chosen ingredients, while guests watched. Not everything was perfect. Twice I did not receive the omelette that I ordered. Once my wife received that and I received the fried eggs the person behind me had ordered. Another time I saw somebody else receive the omelette I had ordered and I received another. Why not be tolerant, if the chef is good humored and the guest is not abused?  I was interested to read another review in which it was said that the staff had received preparatory training in English. They had varying ability, but most knew more English than I knew Spanish, and we could use different languages without grudging. Once I even became a translator for several German children, whose language I could manage, and a Dominican waitress in the buffet.  By the way, guests in the buffet whould not miss the non-smmoking dining room, if that is their preference.

<Author>TandPBoston_NY
<Content>What a beautiful beach! We returned yesterday from LTI Punta Cana and I assure you, you will have a wonderful week if you go there. The beach is beautiful - white sand, and very clean. There are more than enough chairs, and quite a few huts, but you have to be on the beach early for a hut. (Likewise the pool huts.) The pool itself is lovely The staff throughout the resort are extremely helpful and pleasant. Some don't understand English at all, but always try to help. The rooms were very clean, but sometimes our room wouldn't get made up until about 5:00. If you leave little gifts for the cleaning person, you will see a difference in your service! Each room has a mini bar refrigerator that is stocked daily with a gallon of water and two bottles each of 7UP and Pepsi. No alcohol. The best drink is the Bananamomma and it's best if you get it at the el Bucanero restaurant. This resort does not serve frozen drinks and they don't know what you're talking about if you ask for one. They think a frozen drink means 'with ice'. So, forget about frozen daquiris or pina coladas. But, the bananamomma was served frozen on a couple of ocassions. Re the restaurants: el Bucanero is a casual place and has a mixed grill every day. Pork chops, chicken, sausage, ribs, burgers and dogs, sometimes roast beef and fish. The chicken is excellent, the ribs tough but tasty, the beef is always very tough, and I didn't try the burgers but I heard people say they were different. You won't go hungry here. The main buffet restaurant - men cannot wear shorts or flip-flops or they will not let you enter. The food here I found to be not quite as good as other resorts. I also thought the selection was limited. Also, there is a cat that roams this restaurant daily and I didn't like that at all. There are two other restaurants - an Italian (Trattoria) and a seafood, both of which require a reservation for dinner. The Italian is pizza - your choice of many different pizzas, some of which you must pay for. Also there is a tiny buffet with salads and desserts. The seafood restaurant offers a several course dinner with full, excellent service. This is quite a bit more formal than the others. No buffet here and the food is the best of the resort. Several menu items are additional charges. Up the beach just beyond the water sports center, you will find a large group of vendor stands and you can find pretty much anything you're looking for. It's only about a 5 minute (or less) walk up the beach. Be sure to offer them LESS THAN HALF of what they're asking and stick to your guns!!! (For example, I bought a few beach wraps. They quoted me $40 each and I ended up paying $7!) It's a fun time shoppping! The resort had a few power outages during our stay. Usually they didn't last very long. The shows are not worth your time so don't be disappointed if you miss them. We went once and that was enough.All in all, you'll have a good time. Enjoy that beautiful beach!!!

<Content>Great Vacation This was our fourth trip to the D.R and we knew what to expect. We read many reviews on the hotel before we left home. We found the food to be very good and plenty of it. The beach in Punta Cana is nicest beach on the island and runs for miles in both directions. We found a couple of small problems but nothing major. The staff at the front desk could be a little more helpful by not making you wait 5 minutes before they felt like talking to you. Also, they charge you to play pool and table soccer. This is a all inclusive resort, why the charge ? Overall we enjoyed the week at the resort and would recommend it to our friends.

The resort is run by a German company and the German ladies think nothing of going topless in and around the pol and beach. After seeing about 3 topless, I got used to it. Although the little children were completely naked, which I never got use to! The men in all shapes and sizes wear little Speedo suits which now gives my husband his right to wear one on the Jersey shore...beware Americans!!! The language spoken by the staff was Spanish...very little English was spoken...or understood. The housekeeping staff was meticulous and were the rooms. I brought some jewelry that I no longer wear and put the articles in baggies with ribbons attached and gave the girls a present each day. They were delighted and so I was with their expressions! The food was plentiful...if you knew what you were eating. I think they cater to Germans, in the food catagory. I did manage to eat fine and so did my husband, but the kids were a bit more careful. Breakfast was eggs over light, ham..NO bacon, croussants, coffee (too strong for me) orange or pineapple juice. They serves cereals, great pineapples, melons, papaya...no straberries! yogurt and all types of sliced meat, hot and cold German fare. Lunch was pasta, pizza or grilled meats; hot dogs, hamburgers, chicken, french fries. Dinner was okay. We ate at the buffet the first night. Seems like they have the same thing daily. The seafood restaurant was okay...but you had to pay extra for the good stuff. The Italizn restaurant was horrible. All they served was pizza. My husband and I may return again...but without the kids. Not enough night action for them. For us...it was usally in the room by 9 so he could watch ALL the sports on the satellite TV. That really made the rip for him..as for me...my stomach is still queasy!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wouldn't return, wouldn't recommend it. LTI Resort at Punta Cana, Dominican Republic is a nice hotel/resort in terms of accommodations, but I would never return to this, or any Punta Cana resort, nor would I recommend it to anyone. There is plenty of decent food to eat for any diet from carnivore to vegan and everything in between at the four restaurants. (But the selection gets real boring during a week-long stay.) The seafood restaurant is O.K. if you order something on the menu that requires additional payment. The stuff that's included in the all inclusive package on the menu sucked. The Italian restaurant really sucked. Although it advertised pasta and pizza, the only thing on the entire menu were different varieties of pizza, all of which were awful. (I've eaten better frozen pizzas.) The water is only Caribbean tourquoise out to the line of bouys, about 30 or 40 yards off the beach, which you are prohibited from crossing. I never was able to find out from anyone why no one was to ever cross that line, but I've since been advised that it is probably because the water is shark infested. Apparently for that reason, in an entire week, you never saw a single person snorkling or scuba diving out around the reef, probably a couple thousand yards out from the beach. If you look on the map, this eastern end of the Dominican Republic is where the Caribbean Sea and Atlantic Ocean meet, so the water is very disapointing if you've ever been somewhere like Cozumel. The water turns a deep azure green aboout 30-40 yards off the beach. Likewise at the two adjacent resorts on either side of LTI. About 60% of the vacationers are German, (LTI is a German hotel chain), 25% French, and the remianing 15% a mixture of mostly Americans and Canadians. Some staff are fluent in all four languages; German. French, Spanish, and English. The staff are friendly, welcoming and helpful, if you can locate someone who understands the language that you speak. Many of the staff are only fluent in the three languages other than Spanish at the bare survival level necessary in order to successfully do their jobs. There are 39 different resorts on the 27 mile Bavaro Beach. There was no real entertainment, nowhere to go, and nothing to see but the beach. The only things near are the adjacent resorts. (I noticed that one resort on the way to LTI had a casino, which would have been nice.) The national beer, Presidente, is the only beer available. It's a nice, light Pilsner, and quite drinkable from 10 a.m. -2 a.m. daily. Many fruity rum drinks are also in your all-inclusive package. A very limited variety of sold-in-America Brand name liquors are available at an additional charge. There are some gorgeous topless young French women on the beach every day, which was one of the highlights of the entire trip. In summation, the vacation value for the price is quite good, and maybe unmatchable. But if I had it to do over again, I would spend more money and go somewhere much better than this in the Caribbean.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not bad - Not great The Good: It was (relatively) inexpensive compared to other all-inclusive resorts in the area. Presidente beer is exceptional by any standard. The beach was lovely and well maintained. Met some terrific people from Toronto and other parts of the world.The Marginal: The food was plentiful, but not good - even by all-inclusive standards. Clientele is primarily German (manners are clearly optional in Germany.) The staff was friendly, but not overly so, often posturing for tips. Rooms are Spartan, but clean. Little activity outside of the resort; a market with the most aggressive vendors on the planet. Only about 1/2 the staff spoke English.The Bad: The kids club (including the alleged mini-disco) was understaffed and unenthusiastic. Beach activities are limited, and boat rentals and tours are inexplicably expensive. Unlike other nearby resorts there is no beer provided in the rooms. And worse, none of the bars serve Mojitos.The Verdict: Tough call. For the price, the LTI was OK, although I would not choose to go back. I have stayed at/seen other Resorts in Punta Cana and all are superior to LTI. Personally, I would pay more to stay at the Iberostar or again at the RIU Bambu.

<Author>southbound1969
<Content>Nice resort, nice price My wife and I stayed at the LTI Beach Resort 12/05/2003 through 12/11/2003. We arrived just in time for tropical storm Odett, the first storm in the month of December in 54 years I'm told. The weather was lousy for four days but days five and six were almost perfect. The beach is excellent with fine white sand. The water is warm with beautiful turquois water. There were lots of people on the beach but yet it was not overly crowded. The resort is fairly new and is nicely landscaped. The rooms are big and quiet and were spotless. There are plenty of bars scattered around the resort so you never have to go far for a drink. The food ranged from average to excellent. There are buffets and reservation only resaurants to choose from. Entertainment is provided at night and is a bit cheasy but amusing and keeps you busy for a couple of hours. Some of the staff is very friendly while others are just there to do their job. They are just finishing a new building on the property that looks like it will add another 150 rooms or so. Hopefully they will add the appropriate resaurant facilities and beach furniture so the existing facilities are not overrun. The whole Punta Cana area will be very big in a few years as they are in the process of building other resorts and LTI was full when we were there. We would definately recommend this resort to others and plan on returning later if the price is right.

<Content>The best experience!! My boyfriend and I went to Punta Cana last year (Dec. 14, 2002.) I was kind of leary about the hotel because it wasn't very expensive. But much to my surprise, it was awesome. The activity team there is so great, they try to get everyone involved. They teach you dancing, spanish, how to scuba dive, and many other things. The food there was also great, I love to try new things. The shows at night were very entertaining. The beach is also very very beautiful. It is a very good location because there are markets on the beach for shopping and there is also a marketplace close by which is about a five dollar taxi ride. The rooms in the hotel are very nice and clean. Our air conditioning was leaking and we called the front desk and they were there right away to fix it. There really isn't a whole lot to do but it is very relaxing. You can go on all kinds of excursions. We went on the Bavaro Runners for about $55. We got to tour all around Punta Cana and see a typical house, school, ranch, and also a cigar museum. It was very interesting and fun. The artwork there is the most beautiful and you can get a 4foot by 4foot painting for only like $30. All in all I would have to say this is the best trip I have ever been on, and I will definitely go back to LTI!!!!
